Current Situation of Japanese Military Control in the Northeast: Reducing the Strength of the Pseudo-Army; Establishing Air Force Bases 90

Changchun Communication, Japanese military rule in the Northeast has been extremely aggressive recently. The various situations are compiled as follows:

Downsizing the Pseudo-Jing'an Army 91

The pseudo-state's so-called basic army, the pseudo-Jing'an Army, has recently entered the "rabbit dies, the dog cooks" path due to the decline in the strength of the Volunteer Army, and it has been downsized by the Japanese, euphemistically called elite soldiers. The main contents are: (1) Restriction, those with upright character, 18 to 28 years old are qualified. (2) Reduction, the original eight brigades of the first and second armies have been changed to four brigades, a total of four brigades and 700 people have been cut. (3) Salary reduction, those who have not been cut will have their salaries reduced by 10%. (4) Date: To be implemented in mid-October of this year.

Pseudo-Capital Tumen Line Security 92

After the Japanese seized the Northeast, they actively built railways, connecting the Jichang, Jidun, and Duntumen lines, changing them to the Jingtu line, directly to Chongjin, Korea, which can be reached in 24 hours. However, due to the repeated destruction by the Volunteer Army, the line is very heavily guarded. The Changchun Guard Section has 12 Japanese and 257 pseudo-police, a total of 269 people. The Jilin Guard Section has 10 Japanese and 160 pseudo-police, a total of 170 people. The Jiaohe Guard Section has 10 Japanese and 148 pseudo-police, a total of 158 people. The Dunhua Guard Section has 10 Japanese and 173 pseudo-police, a total of 183 people. The Shuangyang Guard Section has 7 Japanese and 74 pseudo-police, a total of 81 people. The Tumen Guard Section has 12 Japanese and 85 pseudo-police, a total of 79 people. In total, there are 61 Japanese and 897 pseudo-police, a total of 958 people.

Completion of the Four Provinces Air Route 93

The Japanese are actively urging the Ministry of Military Affairs and the Ministry of Communications of the puppet army to build air routes and stations, and have completed 3,950 kilometers. The total flight time is 27 hours. On September 6th and 16th of this year, they took off from Jinzhou twice. Each time, a five-plane formation flew around. The first day's journey was between Jinzhou, Tongliao, Zhengjiatun, Taonan, Ang'angxi, and Qiqihar, 800 kilometers. The second day was between Qiqihar, Ang'angxi, Hailar, Manzhouli, Hailar, Ang'angxi, and Qiqihar, 1100 kilometers. The third day was between Qiqihar, Nehe, Nenjiang, Heihe, Hailun, and Harbin, 900 kilometers. The fourth day was between Harbin, Yimianpo, Hailin, Ning'an, Yanji, and Longjing Village, 450 kilometers. The fifth day was between Longjing Village, Hailong, Shenyang, and Jinzhou, 700 kilometers.

Current Situation in Jilin's Military and Political Affairs 94

Regarding all facilities in Jilin under Japanese and puppet state control: (1) Military: 1. In July, it was announced that the puppet state's four provinces would retain a total of 100,000 troops. 2. Each infantry company would consist of 40 officers and soldiers. 3. All brigades would have Japanese instructors. 4. Defense zone assignments would be determined by the Japanese. 5. Various military schools would be established in Changchun, staffed by Japanese instructors. Additionally, concerning military deployments: 1. Attention would be paid to land and water transportation for local convenience. 2. Heavy troops would be stationed near the Russian border. 3. The 10th Japanese Division would be stationed along the wharves of the Songhua River. The first line of defense would be at Fujin, equipped with heavy artillery and an airfield. The second line of defense would be at Jiamusi, with over 300 barracks built by the Japanese, a poison gas training facility, and heavy artillery and an airfield. The third line of defense would be at Yilan, with heavy artillery and an airfield. The fourth line of defense would be at Tonghe, with heavy artillery and an airfield. Japanese troops would also be stationed at Fangzheng and Binzhou. 4. A large amount of fodder would be collected and transported to areas such as Manzhouli, Heihe, and Suifenhe. (2) Police: 1. All county Public Security Bureaus would be renamed Police Affairs Bureaus. 2. Each bureau would have a Japanese training officer. 3. Important matters and financial processing would require the consent of the Japanese. (3) County Administration: 1. Large counties would have two Japanese advisory officers, while small counties would have one. 2. All county affairs would require the advisory officers' approval before being processed. 3. Investigations of intellectuals and household registration checks would be initiated. (4) Education: 1. Enrollment in secondary schools would be reduced. 2. Primary schools would maintain their original state, but textbooks would be revised to remove nationalistic content. 3. Japanese language instruction would be added to all levels of schools, taught by Japanese instructors. 4. School teachers would be required to deliver lectures on Sundays in the streets about the friendly relations between Japan and Manchuria. (5) Transportation: 1. Existing railways would be connected. 2. New railways, such as the Lafa-Bin County and Bin County-Tongjiang lines, would be actively constructed. 3. Trees along the newly constructed roads would be felled by the Japanese army without compensation for use as construction materials. 4. The construction of important rural roads would be underway, with many already completed. 5. Wharves along the Songhua River would be under construction. 6. Shipping on the Songhua River would be reorganized, with one ship operating daily between Harbin and Fuyuan. 7. Each ship would have a Japanese chief steward, and preferential berths would be reserved for Japanese passengers. (6) Currency System: 1. The Central Bank of Manchuria would be established to issue currency for the puppet state of Manchuria. 2. All previously circulating currencies, such as Jilin silver dollars, Jilin notes, Jiang silver dollars, Jiang notes, Fengtian banknotes, and Harbin silver dollars, would be invalidated by June of the following year to implement a unified currency system based on the gold standard of the puppet state of Manchuria's currency. (7) Harmful Influences: 1. Public cultivation, sale, and consumption of opium would be permitted. 2. Gambling dens would be rampant in all cities and towns. 3. Brothels would be found in guesthouses, restaurants, and even bathhouses.

Ethnic Groups in Xinjiang's Troubled Situation: Approximately 2.5 Million in the Entire Province, with the Hui People Holding the Greatest Influence 95

Dihua Correspondence: Xinjiang has a vast area and a sparse population, with a particularly complex mix of ethnicities. Historically, issues in the northwest border region have often stemmed from this complex ethnic makeup, and the current unrest in the province is no exception. The importance of the relationships between these ethnic groups is self-evident. According to a survey conducted in 1922, the total population was approximately 2.5 million, though this figure is unreliable. In recent years, there have been no accurate figures, so it is impossible to know how the population has increased or decreased. Among the various ethnic groups, the Hui people wield the greatest influence, including various groups such as the Inner and Outer Sart, Turkic, Kazakh, Burut, and Gansu Hui. Other groups, such as Han, Manchu, and Mongol, constitute a very small portion of the population. The following is a survey:

Hui People: They are a powerful ethnic group in the province and are quite complex. The Sart, also known as the Kashgar people, are more numerous and reside in the southern region of the Tianshan Mountains. They are of Turkic origin. The Turkic people, also known as the Tajik, and the Kazakh and Burut, mostly reside in the northern region of the Tianshan Mountains.

Han People: They mostly live in Dihua and originate from various inland provinces. They are primarily merchants.

Manchu People: They mostly live in the Yili region and are descendants of those who were relocated there in the past.

Mongol People: They are scattered in the northeastern region and mostly practice Lamaism. Some also follow Islam.

North China's Diplomacy with Japan: The War Zone Issue Is Gradually Being Resolved; Yoshi's Presence in Beiping is Highly Notable 96

Beiping Correspondence: The complex and intricate diplomacy in North China is currently being resolved. Regarding various issues in the war zone, those of a local nature are being discussed by officials from the North China authorities and the Japanese Kwantung Army. For example, bandit suppression in eastern Hebei has been agreed upon. The fact that the security forces were twice obstructed can be seen as an admission by the instigators themselves. They have now been allowed to proceed eastward after reaching a so-called understanding. They have been suppressing bandits for days, and the area near the railway has been pacified. The bandits in Funing are also surrounded and in dire straits, requesting to be incorporated. The return of the various passes along the Great Wall, as well as customs and postal services, is also being discussed. The Japanese Kwantung Army originally intended to send Okamura Yasuji to Beiping again for negotiations, but this plan was temporarily suspended to avoid outside attention. However, in order to understand the situation in Beiping and discuss certain issues, they specially sent a plane from the puppet state's Manchuria Railway Company to Beiping to pick up Shibayama, the military attache of the Japanese embassy, and take him to Changchun for discussions. Shibayama has been gone for two days and has not yet returned to Beiping. The puppet state's Manchuria Railway Company plane has arrived twice, once to pick up Kita Kiyoshi and once to pick up Shibayama. The repeated dispatch of this plane to Beiping by the Japanese is intentionally or unintentionally significant. Tracing back to before the Yuguan Incident, a puppet flag was first hung on a train on the Fengshan Railway, which then proceeded directly to Yuguan. Then, under the pretext of train operations, they occupied the station buildings and raised a puppet flag at Yuguan. Subsequently, they dispatched puppet state police to occupy Yuguan by force. Past events are clear and can be reviewed. The repeated dispatch of the puppet state plane to Beiping, allowing the bizarre and dazzling puppet flag to first appear over the ancient capital, has a purpose that can be inferred.

Since local issues are being discussed with the Japanese Kwantung Army, various issues related to overall diplomacy are also being studied to find solutions. When Japanese envoy Yoshi arrived in Beiping, he stayed indoors to show that he had no role in Beiping. However, the day before yesterday, he met with the authorities, and yesterday, under the guise of recreation, he moved to the Summer Palace to facilitate discussions. Yoshi's main task here is not to solve practical problems but to explore ways to solve them. In reality, if Japan does not abandon its policy of aggression, it will be difficult for our country to achieve good results even through negotiations. (October 26)

Peng Dehuai's Raids on Xiaoshi Suffer a Crushing Defeat; Economic Panic in Bandit Areas Leads to Roadblocks and Forced Donations; Chiang Orders Commendation of the 3rd Security Regiment 97

Nanchang Correspondence: Xiaoshi is the main route to Lichuan. To defend Lichuan, Xiaoshi must be secured. After the recapture of Lichuan, the headquarters immediately telegraphed the entire Huang Division to station there and take charge of security. Many guerrillas and scattered bandits were captured one after another. After bandit leader Peng Dehuai learned of this, he personally led the entire 37th and 25th Corps, as well as a part of the 5th Corps, numbering about 30,000 to 40,000, with about half of them armed, and besieged Xiaoshi on three sides, hoping to cut off the traffic between Nanchang and Lichuan. From the 9th, a portion of the bandits occupied Hongmenshi behind Xiaoshi, another portion cut off communication with Xinfeng, and the main force of the bandit army launched a three-sided encirclement attack on the division's positions. Peng's bandits set up command in a temple on a mountain opposite the town. The Huang Division responded calmly, ordering all officers above the rank of sergeant to perform internal duties and instructing them not to attack until the bandits were within a certain distance. From the evening of the 10th, the bandits launched four or five assaults every night. The Huang Division waited until they were close before opening fire, killing countless bandits. On the night of the 14th, the bandits set fire to the mountains and forests, using the flames to disturb the morale of our troops. Then, Peng personally led a charge. The entire Huang Division fought back. By dawn, the 1st Regiment of the Huang Division broke through and surrounded the right wing of the bandits, killing a bandit army's puppet regimental commander. The bandits' order was greatly disrupted. Peng knew that the situation was hopeless and retreated in panic, abandoning a large number of weapons and ammunition. In summary, the division's defense of Xiaoshi involved five days and nights of hard fighting, resulting in the death of over 1,000 bandits and the capture of over 400. According to the captured prisoners, the number of wounded and escaped bandits was over 2,000. Over 200 rifles and over 1,000 rounds of ammunition were seized. The division also lost one company commander and suffered over 50 casualties among officers and soldiers. Currently, there are no bandit traces in the Hongmenshi and Xiaoshi area.

Military News: According to refugees who recently escaped from bandit areas, the bandits, due to economic panic, have set up checkpoints at various key land and water crossings in the bandit areas and forcibly collect taxes. All goods are subject to taxation. The tax rates are: 2 yuan per 100 jin of tea oil and salt, 8 jiao per shi of rice, and 5 jiao per bolt of cloth. Recently, they also forcibly issued 500,000 yuan in puppet government bonds. All so-called "rich peasants" have their houses, land, and household goods confiscated and are expelled from the area.

Chairman Chiang, upon receiving reports that the 3rd Security Regiment and the Lichuan Guerrilla Force bravely suppressed bandits in the Zuofangwei area near Jinxi, killing many and seizing a large number of firearms and ammunition, issued an order of commendation to encourage them. Yesterday, he specifically telegraphed Chairman Xiong and the general commanders of various routes, instructing them to inform all subordinates. The telegram stated: "Chairman Xiong of Nanchang, General Commander Chen of Xingan, General Commander Zhao of Guangxin: Regarding the recent attack by the 7th Bandit Corps on the 3rd Security Regiment of Jiangxi and the Lichuan Guerrilla Force in the Zuofangwei area near Jinxi, these units bravely fought back, killing many bandits and seizing rifles, machine guns, and other items. They should be commended to encourage them. It is imperative that all subordinates be informed accordingly. Signed: Chiang Kai-shek." (October 24, Datong News Agency)

Four Counties in Western Shandong Appeal for a Swift Plugging of the Changyuan Breach and Request to Be Designated as Extremely Severe Disaster Areas; Representatives from the Four Counties Arrive in Jinan and Will Travel to Beijing and Tianjin 98

Jinan Correspondence: Representatives from the disaster-stricken areas of Puyang, Fanxian, Shouyang, and Yanggu counties in western Shandong, Jiang Mingqian, Liu Qingxi, Zhang Jianling, Tan Xuezhi, Liu Xuting, and others, arrived in Jinan by boat along the Yellow River this morning (25th). They are scheduled to meet with Han Fuju tomorrow to report on the recent disaster situation in these counties and request that he telegraph Yu Xuezhong, the chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, to promptly plug the breach at Changyuan. They also plan to go to Nanjing to present their case to the Yellow River Disaster Relief Commission and finally go to Tianjin to meet with Yu Xuezhong to request the plugging of the Changyuan breach. The representatives are also carrying a petition to the provincial government. According to the representatives, the recent disaster situation in western Shandong and the purpose of their visit to Jinan can be summarized as follows: "We have come to Jinan to request two things: (1) To request the prompt plugging of the breach at Changyuan. Since the project to close the breach at Xiaopangzhuang has already begun, if the breach there is closed, the Yellow River water upstream will flow entirely into Puyang, Fanxian, Shouyang, and Yanggu counties, and our counties will suffer even more severe disasters. Since the frost season has already arrived, the water level has slightly decreased, making the Changyuan breach easier to plug and allowing for twice the result with half the effort. If we wait until the winter flood or spring flood season, the river water will gradually rise, making it difficult to plug. Although the people of the four counties are currently in the disaster area, they can still escape by boat. However, if it freezes in the severe winter, it will be difficult for the disaster victims to escape. If the authorities do not promptly plug the breach now, the four counties may become the new course of the Yellow River in the future. Our visit to Jinan is to meet with Chairman Han, requesting that he telegraph Chairman Yu of Hebei Province, instructing the Hebei River Affairs Bureau to promptly plug the Changyuan breach. (2) The water level in Puyang, Fanxian, Shouyang, and Yanggu counties has not yet receded. The other counties have already planted wheat seeds and can maintain their livelihoods next year. Puyang, Fanxian, Shouyang, and Yanggu counties have not been able to plant wheat seeds, so there will be no harvest next year, and the disaster victims will have no way to maintain their livelihoods. Although our counties have been classified as Class A disaster areas by the Relief Association, the disaster situation is more severe than in other counties, so we specifically request to be classified as extremely severe disaster areas. We will meet with Chairman Han tomorrow, and after obtaining satisfactory results, we will go to Beijing and Nanjing to present our case to the central government and the Yellow River Water Disaster Relief Commission and the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission. After returning to Jinan, we will go to Tianjin to meet with Chairman Yu, requesting that the Changyuan breach be plugged this autumn."

The Petition from the Representatives of the Four Counties to Han Fuju: (1) "Regarding the urgent plea for the rapid blocking of the Yellow River's breach on the north bank to avert a great catastrophe and save the disaster-stricken people. Since the Yellow River breached the north bank of Changyuan County in Hebei Province, the water has poured out, inundating various counties in western Shandong, resulting in an unprecedented and terrible disaster. Fortunately, we have received repeated relief, allowing us to survive. All disaster victims are grateful. However, we recently heard that the construction to block the breach has already started on the south bank, but has not yet begun on the north bank. The disaster victims in the flooded area are eagerly hoping for rescue, and they are greatly disturbed. Now that the frost season has arrived, the water level has slightly decreased. If we take advantage of this opportunity to block the breach, we can achieve twice the result with half the effort, benefiting both the economy and time. If we wait until next year to start construction, after the breach on the south bank is blocked, the river will inevitably flow north, and in the future, during the winter and spring floods, the river water will surge, making it more difficult to manage the breach. If the Yellow River changes its course, the golden dike collapses, and the raging waves surge directly into Tianjin and Beijing, the devastation would be unimaginable. After much deliberation, the people have once again elected representatives to come and present their case, appealing to Your Excellency to quickly find a way to block the breach in Changyuan County to avert a great catastrophe and save the disaster-stricken people. We await your command with utmost supplication." (2) "Regarding the extremely severe disaster situation in Puyang, Fanxian, Shouyang, and Yanggu, where planting is impossible and we appeal for extraordinary relief to save future generations and avoid starvation. The four counties are located in low-lying areas in the middle of the river bend. When the Yellow River breached at Shitou Village in Changyuan this time, the water flooded into the province. At that time, the water depth in the flat areas was more than one zhang. Now that the frost season has arrived, the water is receding, but the water depth in the flat areas of the four counties is still more than five chi, forming a vast expanse of water, like a lake. There are more than 1,400 villages, and over 400,000 disaster victims are still living in the midst of the floods, with no hope of planting and no way to make a living. Among the disaster-stricken counties in western Shandong, this is the most severely affected area. We have received repeated emergency relief, which has allowed us to survive, but it is ultimately a drop in the bucket, only temporarily saving us. Soon it will be freezing winter, and transportation will be cut off. If we do not make plans soon, there will be starvation. Therefore, the representatives of the disaster victims earnestly appeal to Your Excellency to consider classifying Puyang, Fanxian, Shouyang, and Yanggu counties as special disaster areas, providing extraordinary relief to save the hungry and drowning and avert a great catastrophe. We await your command with utmost gratitude." (25th)

Director Zhao of the Jiangsu Finance Department Discusses Relief for Rural Finance; First Borrowing 2 Million Yuan from Various Banks; Government Will Purchase Food or Handle Storage and Pledging 99

The Jiangsu Provincial Government regards the relief of rural finance as the only important political matter at present, and thus established a Rural Finance Relief Committee. According to Zhao Dihua, the director of the Finance Department, the progress of rural financial relief is as follows: It is planned to temporarily raise 2 million yuan by borrowing from banks using a portion of the old land tax arrears from before 1931 as collateral, with 1 million yuan each for Jiangnan and Jiangbei. It will be implemented first in counties with convenient transportation and important towns. The method will be for the government to purchase food, or for banks to handle storage and pledging and establish warehouses. As for the warehouse buildings, existing warehouses and government-owned buildings will be used. Orders have been issued to various counties to quickly investigate and report. Regarding the management of the warehouses, the Finance Department, the county government, and the lending bank will jointly send personnel to be responsible for safekeeping. In addition to the chairman and the heads of the Finance and Construction Departments serving as ex-officio members, the remaining members will be responsible for design and must be experts in rural economics, numbering between nine and eleven people. They are currently being selected and are expected to be officially established around the first of next month. The internal staff will be drawn from the government departments to save money. Although there will inevitably be many difficulties in the implementation of this matter, for the sake of relieving the rural areas, we should design it carefully in order to avoid problems.

Kunshan Youth Comes to Wuxi to Commit Suicide 106

Zhou Quanrong, 26, from Kunshan, was a clerk at the Henglongyong General Merchandise Store in Chenpiao Town, his hometown. His parents passed away three years ago. His brother, Zhou Renrong, is a clerk at the Shixiangji Silk Store at No. 10 Dawangjia Lane in Suzhou. Zhou Quanrong came to Wuxi from Kunshan on the afternoon of the day before yesterday and checked into Room 41 of the Liangxi Hotel on the road, using the alias Wang Shouzhong. He paid two yuan for the room. At around 11 p.m., he went to sleep. At around 10 a.m. yesterday, the waiter Wang Quanlin became suspicious because he had not seen the guest get up for a long time and called out to him without getting a response. He peeked through the window and saw Zhou lying on the bed, his face pale, with black liquid flowing from his mouth. He knew that he had taken poison and immediately reported it to the clerk Zhang Taifei, who broke down the door and entered, only to find that Zhou had already died. He immediately notified Xi Zhiliang, the head of the 13th Tu, who reported it to the county court. Prosecutor Shen led officials to the scene to determine that he had died of poisoning. The hotel was instructed to prepare a coffin for burial. At that time, Zhou Renrong, the deceased's brother, had received the deceased's suicide note in Suzhou and came to Wuxi with his friend Fei Houjun to find him. When they arrived at the hotel, they saw that their brother was about to be put in a coffin, and they couldn't help but burst into tears, a truly tragic sight.

Cai Kunsheng, an account clerk at the Huidatang Pawnshop in Xiatang, Wuyi County, was recently sent by the pawnshop to Liyang to collect debts. After receiving the letter, the pawnshop sent an employee to negotiate, but after waiting for two days and nights, the bandits did not appear. The employee returned to Changzhou on the 26th, and the pawnshop is currently investigating.

Yesterday (26th), Wang Jinwen, a villager, was hired by the Shangmihai Company to transport rice to Shanghai on his boat. Verdict in the Jiangnanpingmou Case in Wujiang 110

Zhang Liu, who opened a pottery shop in Jiangnanpingmou, was strangled to death in this summer by Wu Meisheng, Xiao Hongsheng and Wu Maosheng. They borrowed money using her as a guarantee, stole four pieces of gold jewellery, and were arrested by a road patrol team and sent to the county. They made no defense at the court hearing. Yesterday (26th) the court decided that Wu Meisheng and Xiao Hongsheng had robbed and killed them, each sentenced to death, and Wu Maosheng was sentenced to 15 years' imprisonment. Difficult Livelihood in Jiashan, Elderly Woman Commits Suicide 112

Ni Yonglin, who opened a teahouse in Nanxuan, Fenxing, closed the teahouse due to poor business. After discussing it with his wife, he decided to send his wife to Shanghai to work as a maid so that she could provide wages for the household. When the old mother heard about this, she was heartbroken and thought to herself that she was old and her daughter-in-law was leaving home, and no one was taking care of her. After thinking about it, she thought that she would have to commit suicide to survive, so she took advantage of the opportunity when her son and daughter-in-law were not prepared, sneaked to the Nanxuan City River, threw herself into the river and committed suicide. She was rescued, but had already died.

###嘉興計尚英案移轉管轄

The case of Ji Shangying, a clothing merchant from Pinghu, has been transferred to jurisdiction.

Ji Shangying, a clothing merchant from Pinghu, due to disagreeing with the policies of the former Pinghu County Magistrate Wu Wentai and his personal actions, had listed ten accusations and submitted them to the Department of Civil Affairs. The department delegated an investigation to the county, and all involved parties unanimously denied the accusations. Furthermore, the accuser, Ji Shangying, was unable to provide evidence for each accusation. Therefore, the provincial committee replied that the accusations were untrue, and the Department of Civil Affairs ordered former County Magistrate Wu to investigate Ji. Wu then detained Ji in the county, placing him in shackles and imprisonment. Subsequently, Ji's family requested a transfer of jurisdiction. After much delay, Wu had already left office. Yesterday, the Pinghu County, in accordance with the High Court's ruling, transferred Ji to the Jiaxing Local Branch Court for investigation.

上虞拉夫誤會激成罷市 114

Misunderstanding over conscription in Shangyu leads to a market strike.

On the morning of the 25th, the county government received a telegram from the Department of Civil Affairs, ordering the recruitment and transport of 100 soldiers to the province for deployment to the war zone. At approximately 12:00 PM on the same day, the county defense force's core team and the Public Security Bureau's military police were ordered to begin conscription in the city center. The sudden disorder led to a misunderstanding among the merchants, who believed that this action would greatly affect business as the Autumn Industry and Commerce Recreational Fair on the twelfth day of the ninth lunar month (according to the old calendar) was fast approaching. They gathered at the county chamber of commerce, demanding appropriate guarantees. As Chairman Liu Jie'an and Vice Chairman Zhu Songsan were away in Shanghai for business, the executive committee members Fang Boliang, Fu Ruming, Zhao Qingbao, and Xu Xinifu were publicly elected to go to the county government to request County Magistrate Chen Daxun to stop the conscription. County Magistrate Chen, citing the urgent orders received, was unwilling to abandon the effort for minor issues, lest he delay military affairs. He agreed to allow the release of anyone with a profession who had been wrongly conscripted on bail. As the representatives were about to leave, a soldier of the county defense force's core team, named Jia, refused to release conscripted merchants at the marketplace after repeated requests from the public, and instead lashed out with a whip, provoking public outrage. This led to a market strike. Later, the county magistrate personally persuaded the merchants to open their shops and guaranteed that there would be no more conscription in the city center, and the market then returned to normal.

章振華談暹羅華僑概况　革命四次兵不血刃即告成功　全國商業大權均操華僑之手 120

Zhang Zhenhua Discusses the Situation of Overseas Chinese in Siam: Four Revolutions Succeed Bloodlessly; Overseas Chinese Control Most of the Country's Commerce

Siam is an independent country in Asia. It has recently experienced four revolutionary trends. As the international situation is urgent, all countries are paying attention to it. Recently, Zhang Zhenhua, a prominent overseas Chinese figure in Siam, returned to China for business. Yesterday, he arrived in Shanghai by ship. A reporter from the Min Yan News Agency met with Zhang at his residence and discussed Siam's domestic and foreign affairs and the situation of overseas Chinese. The details are as follows:

四次革命兵不血刃 121

Four Revolutions Without Bloodshed

There have been four revolutions in Siam. The reasons for the revolutions are that Siam's politics are corrupt and society is dark. A group of passionate young people raised the banner of rebellion, and the whole country responded. The revolutions succeeded without bloodshed. However, because the revolutions were not thorough, they were overthrown after being established. This time, the Siamese prince led a large army to Bangkok. Although there was a conflict, the revolutionary army quickly retreated, so the people did not suffer any major losses.

外交政策傾向日本 122

Foreign Policy Leans Towards Japan

The Siamese prince studied in England. Since returning to the country and taking office, he has modeled many political affairs after England. However, due to environmental factors, he is bound by Japan everywhere. All agencies have Japanese advisors, so although there are only 300 Japanese in Siam, they have considerable influence in politics. Even the Siamese king has almost become a puppet. The last time the Siamese king traveled to the United States, he passed through China, but due to Japanese surveillance, he did not go ashore. The last time the League of Nations sanctioned Japan for invading Northeast China, the Siamese representative gave up the right to vote due to this relationship. Most of the current revolutionaries are students who studied in France and are trying to overthrow Japan's potential influence. This time, when the prince led his army to Bangkok, there were also Japanese advisors participating in military affairs.

華僑敎育尚稱發達 123

Overseas Chinese Education is Relatively Developed

The total population of Siam is 20 million, and overseas Chinese account for about one-sixth, totaling 3 million. Overseas Chinese have founded hundreds of schools in Siam. There are 53 schools in Bangkok. The highest institutions of learning are the Zhonghua Middle School and the Overseas Chinese Middle School founded by the General Chamber of Commerce. Overseas Chinese children who continue their studies to seek further education return to China to enter Jinan University, Guangdong's Zhongshan University, and Lingnan University. However, in recent years, Siam has planned to incorporate Chinese people into Siamese nationality, so all schools are forced to learn Siamese, and at a certain age, they must undergo military service.

商業大權均操僑胞 124

Overseas Chinese Control Most of the Country's Commerce

Siam produces abundant rice, and tens of millions of stones are exported to various countries every year. Most of the rice mills in Siam were founded by Chinese. Other timber mills are almost entirely operated by Chinese. Very few Siamese engage in commerce. However, China and Siam have no commercial treaty, so overseas Chinese in Siam have become stateless nationals and are oppressed everywhere. They are subject to various taxes, such as business income tax, head tax, and immigration tax, to extract money from overseas Chinese. Moreover, all business ledgers are required to be in Siamese. Although China has repeatedly negotiated with the country for the past twenty-two years to urge the signing of a commercial treaty, no treaty has been signed to date, leaving 3 million overseas Chinese in Siam without the protection of their home country.

關懷祖國時捐鉅欵 125

Caring for the Motherland, They Often Donate Large Sums

Overseas Chinese in Siam are often oppressed by foreigners, so they are deeply concerned about the situation in their home country. During the great floods in China in 1931, even though the local government ordered them not to donate to disaster relief, most still secretly carried out the donation and transported it to China, amounting to millions. They were particularly enthusiastic about donating to the volunteer army. Unfortunately, China has had many events over the years, and the political situation is not good, so it has failed to protect overseas Chinese who care about their home country. Zhang concluded by saying that his return to China this time is to follow the wishes of the overseas Chinese and urge the government to earnestly negotiate a commercial treaty with Siam, so that 3 million overseas Chinese can receive the benefits of their home country as soon as possible.

中比庚欵委員會奬金論文揭曉　得奬者十五名 126

Five Patrol Ships of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Bureau Departed Yesterday to Protect Fishing; Reiterate Previous Orders Not to Solicit Ocean Protection Fees

鐵路互運材料聯運收費辦法修正　鐵部令各路局遵辦 136

Revised Method of Inter-Railway Transportation of Materials; Ministry of Railways Orders Bureaus to Comply

The Shanghai-Nanjing-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration received instructions from the Ministry of Railways stating that the 16th National Intermodal Transport Conference discussed and resolved the proposal to change the method of charging for inter-railway transportation of materials. The Intermodal Transport Department proposed changing the method of charging for inter-railway transportation of materials in principle. After the Intermodal Transport Department revises all the changed articles, they will be issued to various railway bureaus for trial implementation. The record is on file. The revised text is that the freight rate for inter-railway transportation of materials is calculated at 9 cents per ton per kilometer. All car rental and late fees for inter-railway transportation of materials, track-crossing locomotives, and vehicles will be handled in accordance with the regulations stipulated in this chapter. For inter-railway damaged locomotives and vehicles, the freight will be collected at 4.5 cents per ton per kilometer based on the actual weight of the car body. It should be approved for implementation. In addition to separate orders, it is hereby ordered to comply with this order. This order has been forwarded by the bureau to the Car Department for compliance.

Collection of Tributes

林氏行狀 139

Lin's Deeds

When we read Li Xing's epitaph for Yang Shu, the descriptions of his conduct and Taoist techniques have not been like those of my best friend, Mr. Huanting. The epitaph says that Duke Yang inherited the high style of bravery and integrity, had a good grasp of scale, and was kind and benevolent, just like Mr. Lin's early education at home, knowledge of the country's history, pain over the nation's demise, and following the lead of a mentor, joining the alliance in Yinghai, presiding over the alliance in Vietnam, vowing not to change, and not resting until success, and being upright in mind and gentle in manner, similar to him. The epitaph also says that his ideals and actions were outstanding and not ordinary, that he roamed in mystery and silence, promoted Taoism, and was knowledgeable in the arts, which is even more like Mr. Lin's inherent learning, love of righteousness, and respect for virtue. Mr. Lin connected talents at home and abroad, cultivated voice and strength, assisted the late Premier, gave advice, never changed, and never tired. After Zhennan, and after the establishment of the Republic of China, he never stopped working and never complained, and he never failed to help. It is said in the epitaph that he met the revolution and had a great style, held civil and military power to gather great power, which is indeed the case. However, Mr. Lin did not receive a rank or salary, and only modestly took it as his responsibility to promote party principles and culture, which is different from Shu Zi's career. The epitaph also says that he declined the reward of a great country, disarmed his troops, and declined credit and position, to be carefree in his original good intentions, which is similar to his original aspiration. What we know is that Mr. Lin's scriptures and latitude were precise, the transfer and reception were orderly, the equipment was prepared, and the benefits were transported. The plan was meticulous and never leaked. Since the founding of the country, he has still been in charge of the Department of Civil Affairs, not only not enriching himself, but also not living a comfortable life. He always took every penny to contribute to the overall situation. Looking at his life, his family was bare, with only a few shelves left to recognize Mr. Lin's life. He was exhausted by the party's affairs, not to mention having no time to calm his family, and even his life was never taken into account. He can smile and see the late Premier in the high sky of darkness. The inscription on the epitaph says, "Do without owning, ambition surpasses the clear sky," which is enough to recite for Mr. Lin. Colleagues are not resigned, only follow the shape on the right, the rest is fully biographical, not prepared to write.

Yang, Du, and Wen Went to Suzhou Yesterday and Returned to Shanghai the Same Night

After the Resolution of the Jardine Matheson Stevedore Strike, New Changes Arise: Company Accepts Terms...Compardores Firmly Refuse to Sign...Workers' Morale Surges...A Second Strike Imminent 141

The stevedores of various ships belonging to the British firm Jardine Matheson previously demanded a pay raise, which yielded no results for a long time. On the 21st of this month, they initiated a strike, simultaneously presenting three conditions. Following negotiations by the Preparatory Committee of the Chinese Seamen's Union, the company immediately agreed to accept the conditions. Work resumed the next day, as previously reported. It is now learned that although the company has accepted and acknowledged these terms, and instructed the compradors to handle the matter, the compradors, due to their own vested interests, have refused to sign. The workers are extremely indignant, and a second general strike is about to materialize. The situation is extremely dire. The details are as follows:

Company Accepts Three Conditions 142

On the 21st of this month, after the strike began, the Seamen's Union Preparatory Committee immediately negotiated with Jardine Matheson based on the three conditions proposed by the workers, and promptly invited the company's taipan (chief) to acknowledge them. Therefore, the Seamen's Union Preparatory Committee issued an emergency order that evening, instructing all workers to resume work. The workers unanimously obeyed the order and resumed work the next day. This was the situation at the time of the strike. However, the signing of the conditions was to be executed by the compradors, as the workers were directly employed by them, to comply with procedures. Therefore, the Preparatory Committee originally scheduled to co-sign with the compradors on the 25th of this month. However, the compradors, citing that the wages provided by the company were too low and insufficient to cover expenses, firmly refused to sign on the due date and requested the union to renegotiate and change the conditions. The already resolved labor dispute has thus experienced renewed turbulence.

Compradors Obstruct and Refuse to Sign Agreement 143

However, the Preparatory Committee holds a firm attitude, believing that the compradors' excuse is purely to maintain their own interests and harm the workers. Furthermore, the company has already indicated that the increased wages provided to the compradors are sufficient to accept the workers' conditions, making it clear that the compradors are deliberately obstructing. The committee then questioned the company again. To assume responsibility, the company's taipan, signed a letter to the Seamen's Union Preparatory Committee, stating, "Our company deeply appreciates your association's mediation in the recent dispute between our company's compradors and stevedores. Our company will certainly acknowledge and accept the following requirements (three conditions) and has informed each of our ship compradors to resolve them according to the above articles. Otherwise, please notify our company again."

Workers' Indignation: Another Strike Imminent 144

Upon receiving the above letter from the company, the Seamen's Union Preparatory Committee, in addition to informing the workers to work with peace of mind, continued to urge the compradors to proceed with the signing. However, the compradors consistently used the excuse of limited income and insufficient funds, hoping to shirk responsibility and achieve their goal of changing the conditions. Upon hearing the news, the workers were filled with indignation. Yesterday, they gathered at the union to request instructions, preparing for a second general strike to express their strong opposition and further urge the compradors to realize the situation. However, the union, considering that this matter is of great importance and to avoid escalating the turmoil, issued an emergency notice to the company and the shipping mutual aid association yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM, hoping that they would come to the union to sign the agreement before 12:00 PM this morning to resolve the dispute. Otherwise, the compradors will be fully responsible for any incidents that occur.

The National Postal Workers' General Union's Statement on the Dismissal of a Postal Clerk in Hankou 145

The Hankou Postal Workers' Union has been established for over a year and has been registered with the Hankou Municipal Party Headquarters. Last month, the Hankou Postmaster provoked unrest by refusing to recognize the union. The National Postal Workers' General Union dispatched Lu Jingshi and Zhao Shusheng, and the Ministry of Communications sent Yu Senwen, Director of the Labor Affairs Committee, to mediate and establish seven solutions that were accepted by both parties. Recently, the Hankou Postmaster suddenly dismissed postal clerk Li Liqiang (the current executive member of the Hankou Postal Workers' Union), causing a serious labor dispute. According to responsible persons of the National Postal Workers' General Union yesterday, this incident was caused by the postmaster's illegal actions, which the union resolutely denies. They also showed drafts of telegrams sent to the Hankou Post Office and the Ministry of Communications, which are recorded below for public understanding. The telegram to the Hankou Post Office states: "To Postmaster Liu and Deputy Postmaster of the Hankou Postal Administration, we have investigated that your office punished postal clerk Li Liqiang under the pretext of borrowing the postal staff music team and subsequently dismissed him for disobeying transfer orders. Our association, based on the following reasons: (1) The music team was organized through fundraising by the staff and is not postal property. Therefore, its management is outside the scope of postal regulations. Li Liqiang borrowed the team as a staff member and a long-time member of the team, which is his right. Even if it does not comply with regulations, there is no responsibility in postal administration. Your office's dismissal and demotion based on the regulations is illegal. (2) Executive and supervisory committee members of the postal workers' union cannot be transferred during their term. This was one of the conditions agreed upon with your office in the presence of Mr. Yu Senwen, the special envoy of the Ministry of Communications, when resolving the Hankou postal labor dispute. Li Liqiang is the current executive member of the Hankou Postal Workers' Union. Your office's transfer violates the agreement and is suspected of obstructing union affairs. (3) Li Liqiang was unfairly punished, and your office did not allow him to state his reasons or take leave, even after repeated requests from the union. When Li Liqiang was sent to Shanghai to appeal based on the union's resolution, your office proceeded to dismiss him. Such suppression is procedurally flawed and unacceptable. Based on the above three points, the facts are clear. Our association believes that your office's actions are illegal, deprive employees of their interests, and hinder the progress of union affairs. This is an unfortunate development in the joint effort to save the postal service. Our association deeply regrets this. We deny the above illegal actions of your office and solemnly reserve the right to restore the legitimate rights of our workers that have been deprived. If any disputes arise as a result, your office will bear full responsibility. Sincerely, National Postal Workers' General Union." The message to the Ministry of Communications and the Postal Administration is similar and therefore omitted.

After the Dyeing Industry Stops Dyeing, Capitalists Ask the Silk Industry to Fulfill the Old Agreement; The Union Asks for Settlement of this Month's Liquor Allowance, Which is Not Agreed Upon 146

The silk and cotton dyeing workers have been refusing to dye customers' goods due to the dispute over liquor allowance, which has lasted for almost a week. The labor side requested that this month's liquor allowance be distributed first, and it was heard that a certain workshop had set up a new branch in Kunshan, which may lead to the smuggling of goods for dyeing. It was decided to send personnel to investigate and stop it this morning. Yesterday, the capitalists sent a letter to the Silk Industry Association, requesting that the dyeing fee be settled according to the old agreement, and also stipulated the size. They also replied to the labor side that the distribution of this month's liquor allowance would be postponed. The details are as follows:

Stop Private Dyeing 147

Since the silk and cotton dyeing workers refused to dye customers' goods, a panic occurred due to economic difficulties. They sent a letter to the capitalists requesting the payment of this month's liquor allowance to maintain their livelihood. It was also heard that a certain workshop had recently set up a branch workshop in Kunshan, and it was feared that the original goods of the customers would be shipped to Kunshan for dyeing. Therefore, it was decided to send representatives Shen Shuangxi, Shen Dayi, Tan Borong, Jin Aisheng, and others to investigate and take measures to stop it this morning.

Letter to the Silk Industry 148

The Dyeing Industry Business Improvement Association sent a letter to the Silk Industry Association yesterday, requesting the price to be given according to the original agreement and stipulating the size. The original letter said, "Dear Sirs, We have investigated that the silk and cotton dyeing workers of our dyeing industry have requested to separate the liquor allowance and restore the rights of the old agreement, resulting in a strike. Our association is planning measures to resume work as soon as possible. According to the reply from the silk and cotton dyeing office of the Labor Dyeing Industry Vocational Union, they stated that they will not resume work until the purpose of separating the liquor allowance and restoring the rights of the old agreement is achieved. The attitude is firm, and the situation is serious, with the potential for escalation. The cause of this strike is that many colleagues in your association have not fulfilled the dyeing price agreement signed by the Municipal Government Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce Bureau before 1927, and the unit price of various products of the new Ding Di Pi agreed in 1930. This has caused our industry to painfully cut dyeing prices, which is not enough to compensate for the cost of materials such as pigments, coal, tap water, and labor, resulting in huge losses. This has made it difficult to provide the liquor allowance included in the dyeing price, causing repercussions from the workers. Moreover, your colleagues are inconsistent in settling dyeing prices, resulting in uneven silk prices, disrupting the market, and causing the phenomenon of business decline. In addition, the dyeing price includes the liquor allowance, and there is no fundamental obstacle in the dyeing price agreement for deciding whether to mix or separate. The labor side has the benefit of autonomy. Your association should be clear about this meaning, and immediately separate the liquor allowance and amend the agreement to eliminate labor-capital disputes once and for all. If this strike is not resolved, our association will be torn apart between labor and capital, and the situation will force your industry into a vortex, and we will feel the impact together. Therefore, we request your association to adopt the following conditions and promptly convene a meeting of your colleagues to properly restore the dyeing price agreement of the former agreement and the promised prices of various new products newly ordered, and to earnestly settle the price and fulfill it. At the same time, discuss the provisions of silk feet slightly to maintain costs. If there is any consultation during the meeting, please provide the date of the meeting in advance so that we can send representatives to attend the meeting for consultation and seek a solution as soon as possible and resume work as soon as possible. We would be most grateful."

Letter Reply to the Union 149

In addition, the same industry replied to the union letter, "Dear Sirs, We have received your letter of the 26th of this month, stating that all the workers of your office are in great need of daily expenses during this period, and we request that the liquor allowance be distributed before the 30th of this month, etc. We have approved this. We have investigated that many of our colleagues have not settled their dyeing accounts in the silk industry, and they have not paid for pigments, coal, and other goods. The current economic situation is extremely difficult. Moreover, with the occurrence of this strike, business has been suspended, and the source of economic income has been cut off. The factories have difficulty providing food, and there is a danger that even the cleverest housewives cannot cook. In this state, it is hoped that your workers will understand that the request to distribute the liquor allowance before the 30th of this month is both time-constrained and difficult. Our colleagues have the heart to cut meat to give to others, but they lack the strength. Labor and capital are in this kind of painful environment together and cannot fulfill the request. It is hoped that your office will inform the workers to deeply understand and temporarily suspend their demands. Sincerely."

Customs Administration Sends Personnel to Europe and America for Inspection; Lu Bin and Liu Bingyi to Set Sail Today; Xia Tingyao and Ye Yuanzhang to Europe Within Days 150

China's customs service has always valued talent in its personnel administration, deeply believing that to improve customs affairs, it is essential to have individuals with extensive experience, outstanding abilities, and excellent knowledge to manage them effectively. Therefore, the government has always spared no effort in cultivating customs talent. In recent years, in view of the rapid progress of the world and the ever-changing customs policies of various countries, greater attention should be paid to observation to learn from others. Therefore, the General Commissioner of Customs has been instructed to select senior Chinese customs officers with excellent performance each year, undergo rigorous examinations, and send them to various European and American countries to inspect customs administration. So far, four batches of inspectors have returned to China. In 1929, Pan Xueyu and Li Pengshou were sent to the United States, and Wang Huamin and Jiang Chensheng were sent to the United Kingdom. In 1930, Fang Du and Zhou Bide were sent to France, and Wang Wenju and Zhong Dazhong were sent to Japan. In 1931, Shi Kun and Fan Hao were sent to Germany to inspect customs administration and anti-smuggling systems, and Zhuang Zezhong and Zhang Jiabao were sent to the United States to specialize in the country's anti-smuggling system. In 1932, Liu Qi and Yuan Fuchang were sent to the United Kingdom to specialize in the country's customs appraisal system, and Zuo Zhangjin and Li Baotian were sent to the United States to specialize in the country's customs appraisal system. The four individuals selected this year, Lu Bin and Liu Bingyi, will sail to the United States today on the McKinley. Mr. Lu will inspect the customs and anti-smuggling systems of the United States and Canada, and Mr. Liu will inspect the United States customs statistics system. Xia Tingyao and Ye Yuanzhang will also depart for Europe within days. Mr. Xia will inspect the customs and anti-smuggling systems of the United Kingdom and Germany, and Mr. Ye will inspect the customs statistics system of France. It is said that the four individuals leaving this time are all deeply respected and have been serving in the customs service for nearly 20 years, holding key positions as deputy commissioners in various customs offices. The government and customs authorities have high expectations for this overseas trip, and it is believed that they will return home with honor in the future and make a contribution to China's customs administration. It is also heard that each customs inspector must prepare a report on their findings every three months and submit it to the General Commissioner of Customs, who will then forward it to the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance for review. Therefore, each member sent in the past has been able to work diligently and conscientiously while abroad, conducting on-site inspections, and their work has been very demanding. Their achievements have long been praised by domestic and foreign authorities, and they have been able to live up to the government's expectations.

(1) Mr. Lu Bin (2) Mr. Liu Yuyi (3) Mr. Xia Tingyao (4) Mr. Ye Yuanzhang

The Liquor Industry Federation Asks for Exemption from Registration for Door-to-Door Sales of Local Liquor, and Exemption from Tax Refund and Supplementary Tax Procedures to Stabilize Business 153

The Shanghai-Nanjing-Suzhou Liquor Industry Association Federation telegraphed the Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance and the Jiangsu Stamp Tax and Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau yesterday, stating: "We have recently received a document from Chen Xikang, Han Xingwei, Cen Guangqing, and others, the standing committee members of the Shanghai Soy Sauce and Liquor Industry Association, stating that we have heard rumors that merchants' liquor stocks will be inspected in the coming days, and that registration and tax refund and supplementary tax procedures will be required. Although the authorities have not formally notified our association, most of our members have come to the association to inquire about the truth and stated that inspection, registration, and tax refund and supplementary tax procedures are not necessary for door-to-door sales stores. We have excerpted several reasons below: (1) Local liquor merchants can actually be renamed local liquor door-to-door sales merchants. Because no matter what kind of local liquor, once it enters the liquor and soy sauce stores, it must be opened, mixed, and sold retail. Although there may be sales in the original tank, it is only about one or two out of a thousand, which is the same as the nature of a tobacco shop. It is not dedicated to selling the original tank of local liquor. One should pay attention to this. (2) Soy sauce and liquor stores are engaged in door-to-door sales, so their inventory is naturally limited. There are more than 3,000 soy sauce stores in Shanghai, and the stores are of different sizes. Some stores have only four or five tanks in stock, or ten or more tanks, and at most less than a hundred tanks. If registration is required, the procedures will not only be cumbersome, but the quantity will also be difficult to accurately determine. Because they sell daily and the goods enter and exit irregularly, it depends on the prosperity or decline of the door-to-door sales business. Would it not be unnecessarily troublesome and add nothing to the facts? One should pay attention to this. (3) Tax refunds and supplementary taxes. If these procedures are handled for soy sauce and liquor stores, it will inevitably cause major disputes. Because tax refunds must match the receipt, but soy sauce and liquor stores only have a stamped receipt and no joint slip during the public sales era. In addition, if the white liquor is unloaded, there is no receipt at all. In fact, no tax is evaded. If they are ordered to pay, how can merchants willingly comply? Moreover, the same taxpayer and the same government office, the facts are all there, which can be investigated. How can merchants be forced to suffer this huge loss? If the past is traced, the government office that handled the public sales should share the responsibility, so that justice can be served. Otherwise, soy sauce and liquor merchants will vow not to admit it. One should pay attention to this. (4) The government's method is to eliminate corruption and return every drop of profit to the public. Legitimate merchants who comply with regulations and pay taxes should be given sympathy and not be harassed, so as to stabilize business and cultivate tax sources. Now, the branch bureau measures and affixes stamps, and a special bureau is set up along the way to check and prevent fraud. Is this not thorough enough? Why must the inventory be inspected at door-to-door sales stores? This will only cause merchants to suffer endless harassment. Moreover, Shanghai is a special situation. Will the concessions be inspected at the same time? Where is the so-called fairness? One should pay attention to this. In summary, the situation is very urgent. Therefore, we earnestly present the above and hope that you will forward it to the Taxation Department and the provincial bureau for prompt approval regarding soy sauce and liquor merchants' door-to-door sales of local liquor, and exemption from registration and tax refund and supplementary tax procedures to stabilize business." Upon receipt of this document, in addition to sending a separate telegram, we are sending this express mail for your approval and instructions, so that you can inform us for public convenience. Zhang Dalian, Chairman of the Shanghai-Nanjing-Suzhou Liquor Industry Association Federation.

The Customs Notice on Dredging the Huangpu River in Sections, Dredging Sections 7, 8, and 9 First, Starting from the 26th of this Month 154

Valley Lyon, Harbor Master of the Jianghai Customs, issued Notice No. 18 yesterday for the periodic dredging of the Huangpu River, stating: "Sections 7, 8, and 9 of the Huangpu River now need to be dredged. This project is scheduled to begin on the 26th of this month and will continue until a separate notice is issued to suspend work. It will be carried out in two steps, first on the south side of the above locations, or in the Pudong waterway. During the project, the waterway where the dredgers are moored will be closed to traffic day and night. As for the construction procedure, the buoys Nos. 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, and 11 will be removed first. Once the removal is completed, the south waterway will be closed and work will begin. When the project there is completed, the buoys Nos. 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5 will be removed, and all ships will travel on the south waterway, while the north waterway will be closed to navigation and dredging will begin. All shipping companies should pay special attention to the position of the dredgers (two or more) and the anchors thrown out into the navigable waterway. The dredging work is only within the closed waterway and has clear anchor position markers. All ships should be extremely cautious when approaching the berths on the closed waterway, especially the sides where the dredgers are working properly. Diagrams of this project can be obtained from this department, the Pilotage Association, or the Engineering Office of the Huangpu River Dredging Bureau. All shipping companies are hereby notified."

Zhao Hanqing Will Re-Enter Prison to Serve Out His Unexpired Sentence 159

Zhao Hanqing, a native of Xiaoshan County, Zhejiang Province, once belonged to the political circles and served in the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau. In December of the year before last, he was found by the military police to be privately selling opium raw opium in Zhejiang Province. After being sent to the court for investigation, Zhao was found to be a well-known opium merchant. The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway and the Qiantang River land and water transportation were often frequented by him. Not only did he undermine the opium prohibition in Zhejiang Province, but he also belonged to those who were not afraid of the law. He should be severely punished and sentenced to ten years of imprisonment and sent to prison. When he was imprisoned until May of last year, Zhao begged for bail on the grounds that he was not used to prison life. The court approved the request and ordered a joint guarantee of 8,000 yuan in cash. Therefore, Zhao Jiyun, Zhao's brother, asked Zhang Boliang, a compradore of the Alice Foreign Company at 261 Sichuan Road in Shanghai and a native of Hangzhou, to write a joint guarantee, and he was bailed out. It has been a year and a half since then. However, Zhao Hanqing has since remained at large, and he has not thought about restraining himself from the unexpired sentence. Recently, the Zhejiang Provincial High Court found that both guarantors were at sea, so it sent a letter to the Shanghai First Special District Local Court to assist in bringing the guarantors to justice and strictly ordering them to hand over Zhao for investigation. The two guarantors knew it was difficult to shirk their responsibility, so they truthfully revealed the whereabouts of Zhao, and the court issued an arrest warrant and sent it to the French Concession, together with the French police, to rush to No. 20, Lane 280, Longpo Race Road, to arrest Zhao Hanqing and bring him to court for violating the arrest warrant. The responsibility of the two guarantors was then released. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Tingqi of the First Special Court interrogated him. Wang Yaotang, the lawyer of the police station, stated that the Public Works Bureau had no objection to the transfer of the Zhejiang Provincial Court, and Zhao also wanted to make a statement. Judge Wu then ordered that this was an assistance case and the court would not conduct an inquiry, and immediately ruled that Zhao Hanqing would be detained and await a letter requesting the Zhejiang Provincial High Court to send personnel to take him.

International Trade Bureau Releases Statistics on Siamese Rice Imports 160

According to the Guidance Office of the International Trade Bureau yesterday, China has suffered frequent floods and droughts in recent years, the rural economy has collapsed, and the people's food and farming have become increasingly desolate. The rice production is not enough to meet the demand and relies entirely on large-scale imports of Siamese rice for supply. The statistics for the recent seven years are listed below, and the numbers are quite alarming.

1927: 10,425,818 dan

1928: 8,672,322 dan

1929: 4,750,812 dan

1930: 5,037,201 dan

1931: 8,020,774 dan

1932: 6,437,428 dan

1933 (until September): 6,166,952 dan

Observing the above table, the quantity of Siamese rice imported into China in the past seven years was the largest in 1927. As of September this year, the number has already exceeded 6 million dan. Compared with 1927, the total is expected to be no less than that year.

Lack of Funds Hinders Progress of Industrial Materials Testing Laboratory 163

The Chinese Engineering Society, recognizing the gradual development of industry and commerce in our country and the lack of an industrial materials testing institution, initiated the organization of an Industrial Materials Testing Laboratory in 1924 to support the progress of industry and commerce. After years of preparation, some progress has been made, but due to financial constraints, it has not been possible to achieve completion soon. The Society hopes that enthusiastic individuals from all walks of life will provide substantial assistance to facilitate its early establishment. The Society's recent news is detailed below:

Fundraising: Since the establishment of the Industrial Materials Testing Class, people from all walks of life have enthusiastically donated funds. As of August 20, 1929, a total of over 17,147 yuan has been received. Although this is far from the projected fundraising goal, it has been temporarily suspended due to various reasons. However, to expedite its completion, it still relies on the substantial assistance of people from all walks of life.

Allocation of Funds: The operating expenses of the laboratory, excluding the already purchased land, are tentatively set at 150,000 yuan, with 30,000 yuan for constructing the laboratory building and 120,000 yuan for purchasing various instruments used for testing. Currently, apart from the funds already raised, along with donated materials, totaling approximately 40,000 yuan, there is a shortfall of about 110,000 yuan, which needs to be raised continuously.

Future Work: The future work plan of the laboratory is tentatively divided into two areas: (1) systematically collect and research domestic industrial raw materials; (2) conduct tests on various manufactured products or materials for institutions and manufacturers. Institutions or manufacturers that provide substantial support to the laboratory may, within a certain scope, enter into long-term contracts for long-term testing and various research projects.

Testing and Research: The laboratory's planned testing and research scope covers both mechanical and chemical departments. Upon sufficient funding in the future, electrical, physical, and other departments will be added, and the existing departments will be expanded.

Large Bomb Found in Front of Residence of Prominent Dye Merchant 166

Zhao Pinhou and Zhao Guoting, prominent dye merchants, reside at Nos. 2 to 4 Maigen Road, Kangnaotuo Road, West Shanghai. The residence is elaborately decorated, with pavilions, terraces, and scenic gardens. Recently, the Zhao family has been involved in a inheritance lawsuit, which has been adjudicated by the court. Surprisingly, yesterday morning around 9:30, a large bomb was suddenly discovered at the gate of the residence. Fortunately, before it could explode, it was noticed by the gateman, who quickly filled a water container and submerged the bomb to prevent the explosive power from detonating. He immediately reported it to the police station, who dispatched detectives to investigate and report back to the station. The meaning of this bomb remains unclear. It is rumored that the Zhao family has commercial dealings with a certain foreign national, and it is feared that it may be the work of a patriotic organization. This is noted for future observation.

Famous Work on Chrysanthemums 169

The history of chrysanthemums in China is very long. Since ancient times, there have been hundreds of works on chrysanthemums, focusing on artistic depictions, but generally simplifying cultivation methods and seed selection. As a result, old varieties gradually degenerate, and new varieties are rare. In recent years, chrysanthemum enthusiasts in various provinces have spent exorbitant amounts of money purchasing new varieties. The huge sums spent are truly astonishing. Huang Junshu's book, "Chrysanthemum Mirror," is based on practical experience. Its rich content and detailed records mark a new era for the chrysanthemum-growing community. Two of its distinguishing features are: one, detailed cultivation methods, covering everything from soil storage to fertilizer preparation to irrigation management, divided into over twenty categories, encompassing both ancient and modern knowledge and personal insights. It provides unprecedented detail on protecting flowers from seedlings to flowering, leaving no detail unrecorded, making it an unparalleled work for chrysanthemum growers; and two, seed exposure, the latest seed breeding method, which has not received attention from Chinese people. The book meticulously details the selection, soil storage, sowing, transplanting, fertilizing, and potting, with illustrations for easy understanding. It can be used as a reference for those skilled in chrysanthemum cultivation and as a guide for those who want to learn chrysanthemum growing. It is truly an essential book for flower lovers, with several exquisite illustrations. Each copy costs one yuan, plus postage. Available at the Shen Bao publishing office.

Uncle a Wealthy Merchant, Nephew Impoverished, Nephew Kidnaps His Daughter for Ransom, Extortion Letter Matches Note Found on Him, Police Charge with Enticement and Extortion 171

Cai Yuchao (also known as Hexiao), the owner of Cai Tongde Drugstore, has a beloved daughter named Jufen, who is three years old. On the morning of the 19th of this month, at 10:00 AM, she was taken out shopping by the young servant Xie Baogen, but neither returned. Despite extensive searching, there was no sign of them. After several days, Cai suddenly received a threatening letter signed Xiaoshandong, stating that the child was being held by them and that 35,000 yuan was required for her release. He subsequently received four more similar letters. Cai realized his beloved daughter had been kidnapped and reported it to the Xinzha Police Station. Head Constable Zhao Hehai and Cui Chengke were dispatched to Cai's residence at No. 11, Lane 698, Baike Road, to await news. It so happened that Cai's nephew, Cai Tongqiu, who lives at No. 2 Qiu'an Lane, Changan Road, Zhabei, and is currently unemployed, visited his uncle every day after Cai's daughter went missing to offer condolences. On the 21st, Cai Tongqiu volunteered to contact the kidnappers. The two detectives, seeing his suspicious behavior, detained him and found two notes on him. The handwriting was identical to that of the ransom letters. They were immediately taken to the police station, and Cai Jufen and Xie Baogen were found at his home, along with Cai's wife, Shao. All were taken to the police station and handed over to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. As reported in this newspaper, yesterday morning, Judge Wu Tingqi of the First Special Court continued the trial in the Eighth Criminal Court. Cai Yuchao hired Attorney Gu Gongbing to represent him, and Cai Tongqiu hired Attorney Jiang Baoli for his defense. Police Attorney Wang Yaotang stated that after the case was adjourned, the police handwriting expert Mei Yu identified that the note on the defendant matched the handwriting in the threatening letter. When questioned, Cai Tongqiu confessed that he wrote the five letters and claimed that he initially had no such evil intentions but was overcome by a sudden bad thought and fell into the trap of the law, begging for leniency. Cai Shao denied pre-planning with her husband. The court, seeing that the facts were clear, ordered the commencement of arguments. Police Attorney Wang stated that the defendant did not engage in kidnapping at the time of the crime but only in enticement, and then wrote a letter demanding ransom. Therefore, he had committed the crime of enticement under Article 257 of the Criminal Code and the crime of extortion under Article 370 of the Criminal Code. According to the Criminal Procedure Law, he should be punished for the more serious crime. Attorney Jiang Baoli defended the defendant, stating that the defendant's actions were the result of economic pressure caused by the plaintiff. The plaintiff, owning hundreds of thousands of dollars, not only did not find a suitable job for his unemployed nephew, but even when the defendant borrowed money from the plaintiff, it was only three or five yuan. Therefore, he asked the court to consider the circumstances and give a warning and lenient punishment. Judge Wu then declared the arguments concluded and set the sentencing for October 30.

Ningbo Fellow Association Writes to Jianghai Customs Yesterday to Exempt Fish Tax, Fresh Fish Industry Sends Representatives to Seek Assistance 176

After the Jianghai Customs in this city detained fresh fish shipped from Ningbo to Shanghai, demanding tax payment, representatives of the fresh fish industry, Shen Xianlu and Shen Daqing, went to the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Association to seek assistance. After receiving the letter, the Association wrote to Tang Haian, the superintendent of Jianghai Customs, requesting the prompt release of the detained fresh fish and exemption from tax as per previous practice. A reporter from Heping News has excerpted the original letter as follows: Respected Sir, We recently received a letter from the Ningbo Fresh Fish Industry Association, stating that the industry transports fresh fish between Shanghai and Ningbo to adjust the supply and demand in both places and circulate domestic goods. Ships are loaded daily and rushed to the dawn fish market. Any obstruction will cause the fresh fish to rot. Therefore, customs declaration has been avoided in the past to save procedures. Since the Qing Dynasty Guangxu and Xuantong years, for decades, all Customs Superintendents and Tax Commissioners have known the special difficulties of transporting and selling fresh goods and have been kind, not wanting to impose harsh laws. On the fourth day of this month, Jianghai Customs detained our industry's fresh fish, causing a great impact on our industry. The following is a brief summary of the events: (1) Due to limited resources, fishing boats operating along the coast are old-fashioned sailing ships. With no machines, they rely entirely on wind power. When the south wind blows, they sail to Shanghai; when the west wind blows, they sail to Ningbo. The boats gather together with the wind, so the need for fresh fish in both places is often excessive or insufficient. Too much will easily rot and become waste, and the national nutrition will be lacking. Our industry adjusts the quantity, loading from Ningbo to Shanghai or from Shanghai to Ningbo, circulating domestic goods so that the people always have fresh fish for nutrition. (2) The fish tax has already been exempted. In February of the twentieth year, the National Government issued a general order to exempt all fish and fishing taxes. In the future, no matter what kind of organization, it may not establish new items and collect this tax, in order to comply with the government's intention to eliminate cumbersome procedures and protect the fishing industry. (3) Fishermen risk their lives at sea, mostly Ningbo people from Zhejiang. They rely entirely on the fish market to maintain their livelihoods. The Ningbo Customs is familiar with the local situation, so it has long understood the difficulties of fresh fish transportation. It has not collected this fishing tax to date. (4) Fresh fish is a very perishable item, and its selling time is limited to the moment just before dawn. If this moment is delayed, no one will bother with it, and it will be regarded as waste. Therefore, when the ship docks, these fresh fish must be quickly transported to the fish market. If customs declaration and inspection are required, all procedures are more complicated, and the customs personnel are numerous and may not fully understand the difficult situation. Any delay will affect the future of the fishing industry. (5) Slightly omitted, requesting clarification and transfer to the authorities that when ships transport fresh fish barrels at the Shanghai and Ningbo wharves, the old practice of not adding any additional fees should still be followed. It is learned that Ningbo Fresh Fish Industry representatives Shen Xianlu and Xin Lianqing also visited the Jianghai Customs Superintendent yesterday with a letter of introduction from the Ningbo Fellow Association, stating the difficulties in person.
