The French Concession Yuqing Lane's Rent Reduced by 10% Resolved 178

The commercial properties in Yuqing Lane, located west of Baliqiao Road on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, are owned by Zhou Lianji and managed by accountant Jiang Wanping. This spring, due to the economic downturn and sluggish business along the Avenue Edward VII, the shop tenants gathered to negotiate a reduction in rent. They appointed representatives including Yao Zhaoji of Chungiang Hotel, Jin Hongdong of Guohua Electric Company, Hong Yongyu of Brothers Socks Factory, Zhang Huiqiao of Meifeng Silk Store, Shen Yongkang of Yongkang Sauce Garden, Jiang Maotang of Ruyi Restaurant, and Wang Yongkang of Xie Kangcheng, totaling nine people, to send letters to the landlord and the management, requesting consideration of the difficult economic situation and a reduction of the rent. These representatives personally went to the landlord to petition and negotiate back and forth. The landlord has now accepted the conditions and instructed the representatives to negotiate with accountant Jiang. The following terms have been agreed upon: (1) the original rent will be reduced by 10%; (2) the reduction will take effect from July of this year; (3) the rent reduction period will be two years, after which the rent may be increased if the economy recovers. The representatives convened all tenants yesterday to report on the negotiation process. All tenants approved the agreement and resolved to abide by the above conditions. The representatives will send letters of thanks to the landlord and accountant Jiang, and request a letter to the French Municipal Council to amend the property tax receipts.

The Family Industrial Society Establishes a Children's Dental Hospital 179

During the Children's Memorial Day in April of this year, the Municipal Education Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and Health Bureau jointly organized the Municipal Children's Welfare Committee to establish ordinary and labor nurseries and to formulate all measures for the "Children's Year." Their work is currently underway. The Family Industrial Society has always paid close attention to social welfare. Recognizing the importance of children's dental health, and the fact that Chinese people generally neglect children's dental care, almost 99 out of 100 children have completely decayed teeth. Poor dental health means food cannot be properly chewed and digested, leading to nutritional deficiencies and weakened bodies, posing a great threat to the nation's future generations. The reason for this is that dental equipment is expensive, making dental fees higher than other medical costs. Children often have a dozen or twenty decayed teeth, and the cost of repairing them, even at a minimum of 100 yuan per person, is a burden that many families cannot afford, forcing them to neglect their children's dental health. Since its inception, the Family Industrial Society has aimed to defeat Japanese "King Kong Lion" toothpaste with its "Invincible" brand face powder, which has disappeared from the market. Later, it introduced "Pure White" toothpaste to compete with imported brands, demonstrating its deep commitment to dental health. Therefore, it has resolutely decided to sacrifice a large sum to establish a children's dental hospital. All surgical machinery is designed and manufactured by the Family Industrial Society itself, adhering to the principle of using purely domestic products. The designs were created jointly by Chen Xiaodie and Li Xinfu of the society, with guidance from the Health Bureau, led by dental doctor Su Jielang. Dr. Su, with his extensive knowledge and experience in dentistry, has generously sacrificed personal gain to help the Family Industrial Society carry out its work and serve the community. The hospital will charge each child a fee of two jiao, concerned that offering completely free services might deter those in the upper class from seeking treatment.

Unreasonable Questions from Shantou Citizens Rejecting the Levy of Tax on Foreign Rice Ignored by the National Federation of Commerce 184

According to Shiye News Agency, the National Federation of Commerce, recognizing that low grain prices harm farmers and cause widespread poverty, telegraphed the Executive Yuan, Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Ministry of Finance, and Ministry of Industry of the National Government in July, requesting that import taxes on foreign rice be levied as soon as possible to alleviate people's hardship and safeguard the nation's foundation. The Ministry of Industry replied that the tax levy was temporarily suspended due to Guangdong Province's dissenting opinion. The Federation telegraphed the Guangdong Provincial Government again in early September, requesting its joint support. Provinces such as Anhui, Hunan, Henan, and Hubei, considering the levy of foreign rice tax as an urgent task for rural relief, also unanimously supported and responded. The central government is currently drafting tax regulations and has decided to implement them on New Year's Day next year. It is reported that since the implementation of tax levies in provinces such as Guangdong and Fujian, rice prices have been declining daily. Old rice in rice-producing areas such as Anhui, Hunan, and Guangxi is also being sold, indicating that our country does not lack rice. The levy of tax on foreign rice is an effective measure to protect domestic rice. However, the Federation received a letter yesterday from Chen Jingchu and others of the Shantou Citizens' Association, opposing the levy of foreign rice tax and raising five questions requesting answers. The Federation considers these questions absurd and unworthy of a response and plans to ignore them.

Correspondence courses are available for people in other locations, and free instruction in practical English and Japanese is also provided, which is a rare opportunity. The book is now in print and is soliciting pre-orders. Letters have been received from Hong Kong, Nanyang, Pingjin, and other places, making reservations. Mr. Dai Jitao, Mr. Sun Ke, and other great men of the national government have written inscriptions of praise, indicating its value.

Weather Report 192

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated: cloudy skies or light rain. There is a cyclone in this coastal area, caused by a small low-pressure area forming in the middle reaches of the Yangtze River, which will pass through here at night. The area from the mouth of the Yangtze River to Liaodong will turn to northwest winds, which will intensify. There are moderate northeast seasonal winds in the Taiwan Strait. The weather is bad on the coast of Annam. There is a relatively low pressure northeast of the Pilu Islands. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 p.m. yesterday, the temperature in Shanghai was a high of 76.6 and a low of 52.9. On the same day last year, the high was 68.4 and the low was 57.0.

Educational News

General Regulations of the National Boy Scouts of China from Other Cities 193

The preparatory office of the National Boy Scouts of China, on the 26th of this month, issued the general regulations of the National Boy Scouts of China, which was passed by the central conference on September 26, to the various provincial and municipal level councils and all Boy Scout troops for compliance, and informed the various provincial and municipal party departments for reference. As to when the association will be officially established and the issue of to which department the organization is affiliated, it will be jointly discussed at the next preparatory meeting. The original text of the association's notification to the various provincial and municipal party departments yesterday is as follows: "According to the letter from the secretariat of the central executive committee, the proposal to formulate the general regulations of the National Boy Scouts of China was approved at the 90th standing committee meeting, and the approved full text is enclosed to the local party departments, in order to examine accordingly." It is stated that these general regulations are the fundamental laws and regulations of the National Boy Scouts of China, and their importance is extremely high. The regulations sent by the association are enclosed for examination.

A Brief Account of the Drafting Process of the General Regulations 194

In September 1932, Zhang Daofan, a preparatory committee member and secretary of the National Boy Scouts of China, drafted the initial version. In the same month, it was revised by the 5th preparatory meeting. On April 14, 1933, it was submitted to the first meeting of the Organizational Training Design Committee of the National Boy Scouts of China for review by the organizational group. On the 17th, the 4th general meeting passed the principles of the general regulations of the National Boy Scouts of China, and Gu Shusen, Yan Jialin, and Zhang Jiwu were appointed to draft the text according to the principles. On May 4, it was submitted to the 6th preparatory meeting of the National Boy Scouts of China for initial revision. On May 5, Vice President Dai convened a meeting of the preparatory committee members to discuss and revise it again. On June 8, the 7th preparatory meeting appointed Zhang Jun and Zhao Fansheng to reorganize it. On June 22, the 8th preparatory meeting approved it with Vice President Dai and appointed Gu Shusen, Zhang Jun, and Zhao Fansheng to proofread it. On July 10, Vice President Dai approved it. On September 14, the 10th preparatory meeting made the final revisions. On September 25, it was submitted to the Central Executive Committee. On September 28, it was approved and promulgated by the 90th Standing Committee meeting of the Central Government.

Full Text of the General Regulations

Chapter 1 General Principles 195

Article 1: The Boy Scouts organized by the people of the Republic of China in accordance with these general provisions shall be named the Boy Scouts of China.

Article 2: The Boy Scouts of China aim to develop children's ability to do things, cultivate good habits, elevate their character, enrich their knowledge, strengthen their physique, and become youths of combined wisdom, benevolence, and courage, so as to build a nation based on the Three Principles of the People and lead the world towards universal harmony.

Article 3: The training principles of the Boy Scouts of China are as follows: (1) The Boy Scouts of China take loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, faith, righteousness, and peace as the highest principles of training. (2) Neither individual Boy Scouts nor groups shall participate in political activities in the capacity or name of the Boy Scouts; however, participation as citizens according to the law is not restricted, and personal religious beliefs shall not be interfered with. (3) The Boy Scouts of China should adopt educational principles that are child-centered and modern scientific educational methods, taking the children's living, physiological, and psychological states as the guidelines for implementation of training, so as to cultivate their basic abilities needed to serve the nation, country, and society. (4) Boy Scout training involves learning by doing and doing by learning; therefore, children should be given as many opportunities as possible to have practical contact with nature and society, in order to cultivate their various life skills and proper attitudes towards people and things. (5) Boy Scout training aims to make children self-aware and vigilant, taking serving others as the greatest happiness, and adopting "Be Prepared," "Do a Good Turn Daily," and "Service to Life is the Goal" as their mottoes.

Chapter 2 Oath and Rules of the Boy Scouts of China 196

Article 4: The oath of the Boy Scouts of China is as follows: "I, [Name], swear to follow the teachings of the Founding Father, uphold the rules of the Boy Scouts of China, and devote my life to the following three things: First, to practice the teachings of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, faith, righteousness, and peace, and to be a loyal citizen of the Republic of China; Second, to help others and serve the public at all times and in all places; Third, to strive for the soundness of my own knowledge, morality, and physique."

Article 5: The rules of the Boy Scouts of China are as follows: (1) Honesty: Honesty is the foundation of being a person. Whether in doing things, speaking, or in one's intentions, one must be truthful and not deceive. (2) Loyalty and Filial Piety: One must be loyal to the country and filial to one's parents. (3) Helping Others: Exert oneself to the utmost to help others and do at least one good deed every day, without seeking reward or taking credit. (4) Benevolence and Love: One must be loving to relatives and friends, kind to everyone, and protective of creatures that do not harm people. (5) Etiquette: One must be courteous to others and conduct oneself properly in all interactions. (6) Fairness: One must understand principles, distinguish right from wrong, treat people fairly, and handle matters peacefully. (7) Obedience: One must strictly abide by group discipline and faithfully obey national laws and regulations. (8) Joy: One must always be cheerful and have a smile on one's face, and remain calm in the face of any difficulty. (9) Diligence and Thrift: One must be studious, practice what one learns, be hardworking and able to endure hardship, and not waste time or squander money. (10) Courage: One must resolutely do what is right and not be tempted by profit or cowed by power, regardless of success or failure. (11) Cleanliness: One's body, clothing, residence, and utensils must be clean; one's speech must be careful; and one's heart must be bright and pure. (12) Public Morality: One must cherish public property, protect public interests, and not inconvenience the public for personal gain.

Chapter 3 Categories of the Boy Scouts of China 197

Article 6: Any child of the Republic of China who is twelve years of age or older, volunteers to receive Boy Scout training, and obtains parental permission may join the Boy Scouts of China.

Article 7: The Boy Scouts of China are divided into three levels: junior, intermediate, and senior. The qualification standards for each level and specialist standards will be determined separately.

Article 8: The organization and regulations for Girl Scouts and Cub Scouts will be determined separately.

Chapter 4 Organization and Structure of the Boy Scouts of China 198

Article 9: The structure of the Boy Scouts of China is as follows: A. Type A Structure: 1. Patrol: Six to nine Boy Scouts may form a patrol, led by a Patrol Leader and Assistant Patrol Leader. 2. Troop: Two or three patrols may form a troop, led by a Troop Leader and Assistant Troop Leader. 3. Group: Two or more troops may legally form a Boy Scout group, led by a Group Leader and Assistant Group Leader. B. Type B Structure: 1. Patrol: Six to nine Boy Scouts may form a patrol, led by a Patrol Leader and Assistant Patrol Leader. 2. Group: Three or more patrols may legally form a Boy Scout group, led by a Group Leader and Assistant Group Leader.

Article 10: Any Boy Scout group organized according to law, with a qualified Group Leader and a guarantee of at least one year's expenses, may apply for registration as a Boy Scout group of China according to law.

A Letter Regarding Education in Jiangyin 202

A certain gentleman in the education field, yesterday sent a letter from Chengjiang to a member of the editorial department of this newspaper, detailing the state of education in Jiangyin in recent years, which was quite incisive. We are now publishing it for the attention of those responsible for improving education. The letter reads:

Jiangyin is a place you have visited before and know well. May I describe the current state of education in Jiangyin? I wonder if you will have a sense of comparing the present with the past? In Jiangyin, in addition to Nanjing Advanced Normal School, there are county-run schools such as Jiyang (also known as Liyan) Academy, Xijiao Academy, and Liangfeng Academy. Although the assets of these academies cannot compare with Nanjing Advanced Normal School, the larger ones have thousands of acres of land, and the smaller ones have no less than five or six hundred acres. As for the number of charitable schools and literary societies, and the abundance of public funds for scholars, it can be said to be unique in the entire province. The land assets of each charitable school and literary society are at least dozens of acres, and many are two or three hundred acres. These assets provide funding for successful candidates in the imperial examinations, tribute students, and for the expenses of successful candidates and public funds for scholars, as well as providing accommodation for students taking the county and prefectural examinations. In addition to the land for public funds, there are also assets for the two examination halls in the southeastern and western countryside. In total, the assets for education in the county amount to no less than 20,000 acres in the Cao and Sha areas. Combining this with the educational surtax on land and the donations collected from students in recent years, Jiangyin should have no concerns about the lack of funding for education. However, those who collect land taxes are all skilled in fraud. They take advantage of the frequent changes in the names of collection agencies and the lack of unified authority. Coupled with years of poor harvests and low grain prices, they invariably claim that the people are in arrears and massively embezzle the educational surtax on land that should have been collected over the years, amounting to more than 300,000 yuan. Is it truly the people who are in arrears? The school land has been seized and divided by powerful individuals in various towns and villages. Some have hidden it as their own private property, some have sold it and diverted the funds, and some have converted it into the foundation for private schools. The collected land rent is neither reported nor audited, and no one dares to inquire about it. If provincial inspectors come to request the account books for inspection, the cunning ones will invariably use the excuse of fearing that the funds will be taken over by the county for unified management, and delay submitting them, as if they can dispose of public funds without the government being able to inquire. The submitted rental registers are mostly copies, and accounts of tenants who have not paid rent are everywhere. Among them, there are one or two people managing thirty or forty acres of school land and receiving more than three hundred yuan in rent per year. Comparing this with the others, are the so-called arrears really in arrears? The people handling the funds only care about their own well-being. It is no wonder that the annual budgeted income of more than 200,000 yuan is not enough to cover the annual expenditure of 140,000 yuan and still feels insufficient, resulting in arrears of six or seven months of funding for various schools and halls. Those who control the school land in the towns and villages not only profit from it but also control the appointment and dismissal of principals and teachers within their sphere of power. Those who are not of their kind are not allowed to join them, as their embezzlement is easily exposed. As a result, unqualified individuals are allowed to muddle through, and unqualified teachers fill the schools. With such management, it is difficult to talk about results. Therefore, although there are no fewer than 350 schools in the county, with more than 400 classes, the number of children enrolled should reach 20,000 to 30,000. However, most of the village schools have few students and are nominal. The summer vacation has not been shortened, and there are no measures for make-up classes. As soon as they hear that a provincial inspector is coming to the county, they rush to report false holidays, giving the provincial inspector the cold shoulder. They think they have succeeded, but how can they not feel guilty about delaying the children's education? Is this how teachers should behave? Alas, to run education in this way, it would be better not to run it at all! (Below omitted) October 25th.

Fashion Special Issue, Issue 8

Fashion on the Head 237

— You Xing

Just like the buildings in Shanghai, although Shanghai fashion changes faster than houses are rebuilt, it has never achieved its own unique style! The people of Shanghai are extremely busy, and everyone feels satisfied if the number of manufacturers and fashion stores keeps increasing.

Naturally, due to Shanghai's position, it is impossible to reject foreign influences on life in all aspects. Therefore, the so-called "own" characteristics are easily eliminated and difficult to regenerate. But isn't the cheongsam with a high collar and high slits called Shanghai fashion? Now let's talk about this kind of fashion:

Originally, there was no habit of wearing hats, and there was also a head of wavy, beautiful hair. Ladies and women were not afraid of sun or wind, so Shanghai fashion lacked half of its creative work! The changes in the cheongsam itself could not escape the collar, length, sleeve length, and the raising or lowering of the slits, longer or shorter lengths, plus a little arrangement of buttons and the width of the edging. Shanghai fashion also saves a lot of tailoring work! Therefore, the quality of the fabric directly affects the beauty of the fashion; and the choice of patterns on the fabric is even more important than the tailoring! Don't all ladies and women personally go to large companies or silk shops to choose the most fashionable fabrics and then go home and ask a tailor to make them?

This way of talking is not intentionally criticizing Shanghai fashion, but rather hoping that Shanghai ladies will pay attention to this issue: Do we need to wear hats? Are there any shortcomings in the popular tailoring methods? How to modify them? What standards should be used for choosing fabrics? The purpose of this discussion is to try to raise some questions and respectfully ask the ladies of Shanghai to put the effort they put into choosing fabric patterns into personally creating or building new tailoring methods, and to take the time to study "fashion on the head" (growing hair? wearing a bun? wearing a hat? tying a knot? ...). It is not necessary to adopt the styles of European and American fashion, but it is possible to imitate their efforts in studying fashion. From this, we can obtain, like the new City Hall building in architecture, a relatively "perfect" and "own" Shanghai fashion.

The Impact of Fashion on the Economy, Continued 238

— Xu Tao

Peculiar Interests, Frantic Decoration

The Popularization of Fashion

In terms of materials, due to the excessive consumption of decorations, almost all beneficial birds and animals have been destroyed, because some types of fur are becoming extinct. Therefore, there is a desire to raise birds and animals artificially or to limit and protect hunting through regulations. For example, modern European and American women's shoes, handbags, wallets, etc., all love to use crocodile skin. It is said that these animals are almost completely extinct in South America.

Modern industrial economics are making products increasingly popular; fashion certainly cannot escape this trend. From a social perspective, this is indeed a matter of great concern. Because this trend can lead to a large volume of consumption and reduced costs, which allows large industries to exist. In industry, the need to create cheap goods is necessary. Current fashion is not only for wealthy women, but also to allow all women in society to dress fashionably. Everyone wants their women and children to dress beautifully; maybe they even want them to dress better!

Also, clothing with environmental, regional, and custom colors has great historical value; however, in recent years, due to the uniformity and universality of fashion, it has gradually disappeared. At the same time, national borders may also be completely broken down. For example, the clothing of men and women in the country is rapidly becoming Westernized; there is a trend of only wearing and using Western things.

Recent News of Changes in Women's Clothing - Editor's Report 239

In the past, because the slits of the cheongsams were very high, except for bare legs in the summer, women wore long and brightly colored silk trousers with large leg openings, and the leg openings were decorated with beautiful lace; but recently, because the slits of the cheongsams have suddenly been shortened, only opening eight inches, those long trousers have been overthrown and replaced with short trousers.

In the previous issue, the editor reported that quilted cheongsams and fur-lined robes no longer had lace on the hems; however, in the past week, many modern ladies seen in social settings were wearing quilted cheongsams and fur-lined robes in a light lake blue color, and the lining was completely sewn to the outer fabric, unlike the first half of the year. (In the first half of the year, the lining of the robes was not sewn to the outer fabric.)

The copper-buttoned tweed overcoat with military colors was originally created by movie star Tan Xuerong last year, and everyone imitated it, making it popular for a while; however, this year, the most modern ladies have slightly changed the coat. The buttons have been changed to silk inlaid with mother-of-pearl that is darker than the color of the coat fabric; the hem of the coat is wider than last year; the belt is also made of wool that is darker than the color of the coat fabric; and a scarf made of the same color and material wool as the belt is also attached to the collar, which can be wrapped around the back.

According to news from fur merchants, the popular mass-market black leather triangle coats of last year are probably no longer popular this year; because this year, many modern ladies have bought badger fur to make coats (or leather woven with badger fur), and have used black silk ear-shaped fox scarves around their necks instead.

Newly Popular Cheongsams 240

— Yuquan

Recently, some people have used dark-colored pure wrinkled crepe to make cheongsams, with lotus-leaf-edged silk crepe on the cuffs, and the collar, lapels, and hem are inlaid with a black flat piping, and a wide silk edge is attached five and a half inches above the hem. The slits are still open two feet high. A short cape of satin is added to the cheongsam, which feels grand and luxurious.

Black Sheep at the Entrance of the Cave (Part 1) 241

— Lingyun

My old friend Li Xianhuang is a big fat man. On the day of the Beginning of Summer, his whole family was weighed. Everyone else was weighed properly, some seventy catties, some eighty catties, and it was done in a while. Only when it was his turn to be weighed, the scale button rope broke twice, and he never succeeded in being weighed. His wife came up with an idea, picked up a thick lead wire, tied the hemp rope, and hung it firmly on the scale, so that the matter could barely be carried out. However, the weight kept pushing towards the scale tip, until the star marks at one hundred and forty-three catties were reached, and the scale bar above Xianhuang's head was level.

Because he was obese, he was very tired when he walked. If he walked from the bottom to the third floor, he had to rest for at least two minutes before his panting subsided. Because he felt that the long gown and mandarin jacket were inconvenient to wear, and his belly was big, the middle of the long gown often bulged roundly, like a watermelon placed on the table in summer, covered with a towel, drooping on both sides, and towering in the middle, which was very unsightly. Therefore, Xianhuang usually wore Western-style clothes, first because they were economical, and second because they were convenient. He was always very happy to meet friends. When others wore Western clothes, he always added two conditions in his introduction: the waist of the trousers must be made looser, especially the front and rear of the hips must not be too narrow. If the person being introduced was also a fat comrade, he honestly advised him to make two pairs of trousers.

I met Xianhuang almost every other day. I remember last winter, once I saw him wearing a navy blue serge suit, but the trousers were gray gabardine. I asked him, "Why are you wearing two colors again?" He said, "Don't mention it. I've only worn this serge suit for three months, and the crotch is broken again." As he spoke, he raised his leg and pointed to the broken place. I said, "Of course, that's because it's too tight." He said, "Nine out of ten of my trousers have this problem." He sighed from time to time as he spoke, and then said, "It's convenient to wear Western clothes, but if this hurdle can't be broken, big guys are too uneconomical. I hope the Western devils will step up their improvements to benefit fat people." After he finished speaking, everyone laughed!

Zhang Yipeng's Humorous Speech on Fashion in Suzhou 242

— Lili

In recent years, the clothing of women in Suzhou has gradually become Shanghai-ized. Therefore, new fashions in Shanghai often become popular in Suzhou in just a few days. However, since the demolition of the soil hills in the North Bureau of Suzhou, which have been transformed into singing halls and theaters, and since the opening of Hulong Street and Guanqian Street as roads, all popular items have been concentrated here. The prosperity of Changmen in the past has gradually declined, so the clothing in the Changmen area and the clothing in the Guanqian area have gradually become somewhat different. Changmen still retains its original literary talent, while Guanqian is very prosperous and has become a budding Shanghai-ized area.

Recently, the Shanghai Meiya Silk Weaving Factory and the Gantaixiang and Tongrenhe silk and satin shops in Suzhou held a three-day domestic silk and satin fashion show in the auditorium of the Suzhou YMCA. Because it was a first in Suzhou, it caused a sensation throughout the city. Some ladies and women brought bread and pastries as early as 11:00 AM to rush to the venue, willing to wait until the 2:00 PM opening of the show. The YMCA auditorium originally had only 400 seats, but each show was packed with 700 to 800 people, and there were many more people crowded outside the venue who could not get in.

Zhang Yipeng gave a speech on stage on the opening day, which was the most passionate and慷慨激昂. He compared domestic silk and satin to his own children and his own wife. He said, "We love our own children more than other people's children, no matter whether they are born handsome or whether they study hard, because they are our own children; we also love our wives very much, no matter whether they are beautiful or capable in managing the household, because she is my own wife. Therefore, domestic silk and satin are our own raw materials made by the Chinese ourselves, so we should love to wear them. What's more, how can people not love to use such good silk and satin from the Meiya factory?" Mr. Zhang Yipeng's beard and hair were already white, but his conversation was vivid, so he drew applause and laughter from the entire audience.

In the venue, many beautiful ladies were already looking at the various silks and satins displayed in the venue, and immediately bought them back to make new clothes and then came to the show again. Pure wrinkled crepe was probably the most worn by both men and women, and silk crepe was also popular. Many people also used silk satin to make coats.

At first, some people suspected that the fashion styles displayed were only meant to show novelty and were of no other use. Later, someone on stage explained each piece of fashion in detail, explaining why the crepe part was for what, what the effect of the short puff sleeves was, what the reason was for attaching a lotus leaf edge, and how the color matching was related to the seasons and festivals. There was no point that was not carefully considered. Everyone then understood that the fashion was indeed suitable for the season, age, body type, and environment, and was completely rationalized clothing, not just for showing off.

Before the performance, some people also misunderstood the purpose of coming to the show, which was to see the few female stars performing on stage, but Zhang Yipeng also explained that the performers were only sacrificing their appearance as a clothes rack because of the promotion of domestic goods, which everyone also understood very well.

Radio Weekly

Volume Adjustment Method 243

— Li Yuanqing

The volume of a radio is, of course, better the louder it is. However, in the following circumstances, it is necessary to apply appropriate restraint:

(1) To obtain undistorted sound.

(2) In public residences or densely populated areas.

(3) Late at night and early in the morning.

There are indeed many ways to adjust the volume, but very few are suitable for all conditions. This article details various adjustment methods and adds simple comments.

Increasing or decreasing the filament voltage to adjust the volume is the simplest and most economical method (see Figure 1A). However, on the one hand, increasing or decreasing the filament voltage, and on the other hand, keeping the screen voltage constant, then the electrons emitted from the filament are either too many or too few. As a result, the resulting sound waves are inevitably distorted. (This method is not applicable in AC radios, because the filament temperature of AC vacuum tubes increases or decreases very slowly.)

Connecting a variable resistor in parallel with the antenna circuit (as in Figure 1B) to adjust the volume can indeed avoid distortion. However, it cannot be applied in areas near strong broadcasting stations where it is possible to listen without an antenna.

Adding a variable resistor in the grid circuit can also adjust the volume (as in Figure 1C, D). However, adding many resistors to the tuning section will have a significant impact on selectivity.

Increasing or decreasing the amount of regeneration can sometimes also adjust the volume (as in Figure 1E). However, the range of rotation is limited, making it inconvenient to use. Too little and there is no sound, too much and it is easy to oscillate, disturbing the original sound.

Increasing or decreasing the screen voltage to adjust the volume is quite satisfactory (as in Figure 1F). BP is a bypass capacitor; adding it can avoid noise.

Connecting a variable resistor in series in the screen grid circuit is considered the most common and perfect method. Many radios sold on the market now use this method (as in Figure 1G) (To be continued)

How to Use a DC Voltmeter to Measure AC Voltage 244

— Yizhi

We know that DC voltmeters can only measure DC voltage. If you want to measure AC voltage, you must have an AC voltmeter. But now there is a simple method that can be used to use a DC voltmeter as an AC voltmeter. One meter for two purposes can save you from buying an AC voltmeter.

The reason why a DC voltmeter can measure AC voltage is that it uses the principle of rectification. The manufacturing method is very simple. The wiring method is shown in the figure. In addition to the existing DC voltage, only a dual- or triode vacuum tube is needed. The filament power supply of this tube can be supplied by dry batteries, storage batteries, or AC power. When in use, the voltage reading on the meter should be multiplied by a previously verified voltage multiplication factor (that is, the multiple of the difference between AC voltage and DC voltage. This number depends on the screen current, screen resistance, and meter impedance of the vacuum tube used. Because the voltmeter and vacuum tube used are different, the voltage multiplication factor must be verified for the first time). The product is the AC voltage value.

The author has a Weston Model 506, 0-15 Volts DC voltmeter. He used a 280 rectifier tube to connect it according to the figure to measure AC voltage. The voltage multiplication factor is 2.7. If a 201 tube is used, the voltage multiplication factor should be 3.3. For example, using a 280 rectifier tube for rectification to measure a certain AC circuit, the reading on the meter is 8 volts, then the voltage of this AC circuit is 8 X 2.7 = 21.6 volts (approximately).

The voltage multiplication factor is inversely proportional to the sensitivity of the meter. The more sensitive the meter, the smaller the multiplication factor and the greater the accuracy. Therefore, if you want to measure the correct voltage value in an AC circuit, it is best to use a sensitive and high-impedance DC meter. This point needs to be stated incidentally, so I will describe it.

High-Frequency Amplification of Transmitters (Continued) 245

— Ming Xiang

Class B amplification has no screen current when there is no excitation (of course, there is also no grid current), as mentioned above. Now, the oscillation stage is turned on, so that it forms a very loose coupling with the amplification stage. Then the input excitation voltage is extremely small, represented by curve A (figure see previous issue). At this time, the amplification stage has a very small screen current, but the grid current is still zero, because the excitation voltage is smaller than the original grid bias. Curve B represents the highest value of the excitation voltage, which is equal to the grid bias voltage. This is the point where the grid current is about to start flowing. If the coupling is firm, the excitation voltage can be made to exceed voltage C and generate grid current (when the shadow part of curve C). The grid current flows into the C battery, which is equivalent to charging the C battery. The reading on the grid current meter is its charging rate. If a resistor is connected in the C battery circuit, when the grid current flows through it, a voltage drop will inevitably occur across this resistor. This resistor is known as the grid leak GL. Its function is to help supply the grid bias. If only the voltage drop of the grid leak is used to supply the grid bias, and the C battery is not used, true class B amplification cannot be obtained. Because when the excitation is removed, the grid current stops, and the grid leak will of course not be able to produce a voltage drop to completely cut off the screen current. The last question is: How much grid bias is required for class B amplification? It can be calculated using the formula grid bias = 丨P/ц丨, Eb is the screen voltage, and ц is the vacuum tube amplification factor (which can be found on the vacuum tube characteristic table). After the grid bias is known, the resistance of the grid leak can be calculated according to Ohm's law: Grid leak = 丨E/I丨, where E is the grid bias, and I is the current indicated by the grid current meter.

The adjustment and compensation method of the amplification stage has been seen in this journal in the article "Adjustment Method and Steps of Shortwave Transmitters", so I will not repeat it. (The End)

Random Musings (2) 246

— Micro-thoughts

丨丨The Current State of Broadcasting in the Country丨丨

Nanjing

But in fact, there are still many listeners in Nanjing who enjoy receiving broadcasts from Shanghai and Hangzhou. What is the reason for this? It is because: (1) "The love of the new and the dislike of the old" is a common human trait. For example, Nanjing pressed duck is certainly fatty and delicious, but eating it too much can make it feel bland and tasteless. The mouth and ears both belong to the five senses, and similarly, people get tired of listening to the same sound all the time.

(2) The station is directly under the Chinese Nationalist Party and is the only propaganda organ under party rule. Its stance and position are absolutely different from ordinary commercial or privately researched broadcasting stations. Therefore, it has a considerable range for the selection and direction of programs.

(3) Nanjing is a political rather than a commercial area. There are not many entertainment venues, making it very difficult to collect entertainment programs.

Now, within the possible scope, I would like to put forward two points as a humble offering to the station:

(1) Using radio to promote sports was indeed initiated by this station in the country. However, the broadcasting of national martial arts or morning exercises every morning is somewhat rigid and monotonous. This summer, the author heard a broadcasting station established by foreigners in Shanghai, which included light and beautiful Western music when broadcasting morning exercises. Listeners heard slogans such as "Up, down, left, right" on the one hand, and melodious and pleasant music on the other, which certainly made them feel supremely happy. If the station could imitate this approach, it would greatly increase the interest of the audience.

(2) Many people need some kind of entertainment after dinner to adjust their daily mechanical lives, so the station's music program from 12:00 to 1:00 pm is most welcome by the audience. Similarly, it is hoped that the station can also appropriately extend the duration of the music program from 6:00 to 6:30 pm every night.

It is said that the station has long considered laying special lines between Nanjing and Shanghai to enrich the program, but this has not been realized for the time being due to the high cost of equipment. If this plan can become a reality in the future, it will certainly make a special contribution in terms of programming.

Common Sense 247

— Huang Jiancun

(17) Overview of Vacuum Tubes (1)

(1) Overview: Vacuum tubes are to radio as the heart is to the human body. Everyone knows how important they are. Without the invention of the vacuum tube, the development of radio could not have reached its current peak. Today, the manufacture of vacuum tubes is constantly changing. First, there were diodes and then triodes, followed by tetrodes and pentodes, and then all kinds of new tubes that have recently appeared, with innovative patterns and a wide variety of types. There are so many types that we are almost overwhelmed. Here is a brief description of their types and content.

(2) Diode Vacuum Tube: As shown in the figure above, (a) is the general symbol for a diode vacuum tube, and (b) is its cross-sectional view. The tube is equipped with two electrodes: a filament and a plate, inside a high-vacuum glass tube. The filament is also known as the cathode. When electricity is applied to the filament, the filament emits negative electrons due to heat. The plate is also known as the anode, and its function is to absorb electrons. If the plate is connected to a positive charge, it can absorb the electrons emitted by the filament, and at the same time, a current (commonly known as plate current) flows from the plate to the filament. If the plate is connected to a negative charge, it cannot absorb electrons, so no current can flow. The rectifier tube used in AC radios is made using this principle. Therefore, diode vacuum tubes can perform rectification and detection. However, the sensitivity of using a diode for detection is far less than that of using a triode, so almost no one uses diodes for detection today.

(3) Triode Vacuum Tube: The above figure (c) is the general symbol of a triode vacuum tube, and (d) is its cross-sectional shape. The difference between a triode and a diode is that the former has an additional grid. As shown in the figure, the grid is located between the filament and the plate, and its function is to limit the flow of plate current into the filament, that is, the change in the grid voltage can increase or decrease the plate current. Moreover, although the voltage supplied to the grid is small and the current is weak, the change in plate current is considerably increased. This is because the vacuum tube has an amplification effect and can be used for high-frequency and audio-frequency amplification. In addition, the main functions of triodes are rectification, detection, oscillation, and amplitude modulation.

Page 19

Spring and Autumn

Carrying a Lantern Under the Moon 248

— Zhan Lu

It's not me talking nonsense. The Guangzhou Municipality's National Air Defense and Rescue Lantern Parade was held on a moonlit night during the Mid-Autumn Festival. More than sixty groups, with about five or six thousand people, actually had more than three thousand airplanes and more than one thousand anti-aircraft guns parading together. This is a vivid record in the Guangzhou newspapers.

Huh! Does China even have more than three thousand airplanes and more than one thousand anti-aircraft guns? Maybe I misread it and saw the character "ten" (十) as "thousand" (千). But, after rubbing my eyes, it's clearly "more than three thousand airplanes" and "more than one thousand guns." It's clearly "airplanes" and "anti-aircraft guns." The newspaper didn't misprint the type, and I wasn't seeing things. Okay! Okay! A corner of Guangzhou has this amazing number of airplanes and anti-aircraft guns. If we calculate ten Guangzhous for all the cities in the country, then there should be more than thirty thousand airplanes and more than ten thousand anti-aircraft guns. Then, China's air force is the best in the world, and China's air defense force is also the best in the world. Its international standing can leap ten thousand feet. Just wipe your nose and say in a classical style, "Isn't that delightful?" Ah, "Isn't that delightful?"

However, after looking closely, I found the problem. It turns out I overlooked a few words in the newspaper. The newspaper wrote: "Various groups crafted more than three thousand airplanes and more than one thousand anti-aircraft guns. There were about one thousand kinds of paper lanterns and gauze lanterns, and each lantern was written with the four characters 'National Air Defense and Rescue'." So that's how it is, more things made of paper and paste.

I have said in this column before that Chinese science is not backward. Only the paste doctors in the "exquisite" paper shops are showing off. The Guangzhou Municipality's National Air Defense and Rescue Lantern Parade is nothing more than a paste doctor showing off. This year, Su and Hu areas spent the Mid-Autumn Festival on rainy nights. Guangzhou's Mid-Autumn Festival night was moonlit and clear, but it held such a grand lantern parade with three thousand airplanes and more than one thousand anti-aircraft guns. It perfectly corresponds to a Su and Hu slang saying, "Carrying a lantern under the moon, shining in vain." 丨丨 The "shine" (明) is a homophone for "name" (名).

Unofficial Records of Taiwan 249

— Yan Qiao

In the middle of summer, my friend Wang Peizheng asked me if I had seen a classical Chinese historical novel like the "History Hidden in Bookshelves" called "Unofficial Records of Taiwan." I said no, and I checked several books on textual research of novels, but I didn't find this book title, so I assumed it was a unique copy. His friend spent seventy dollars to buy nine copies (missing one), so it wasn't a bad deal.

Recently, I happened to browse through "A Compendium of Notes and Novels" published by Civilization Book Company, and I found "Unofficial Records of Taiwan" in the fourth series. It had the same appearance as described by my friend Peizheng. It was written by Jiang Risheng from Zhupu, Fujian. According to Chen Qiyong's preface written in the year of Jia Shen, Kangxi (42nd year): "I, the priest of Nanzhao, met Jiang Zidongxu from Jiaojiang in the spring of Yichou (24th year of Kangxi). He was a gentle, honest, knowledgeable gentleman. Later, he published his compiled 'Unofficial Records of Taiwan' in thirty volumes. ... It was written specifically for the Zheng family. ... This book uses Fujianese people to talk about Fujianese affairs, detailing the beginning and the end, widely collecting materials, and differing from unofficial novels. It can certainly be used for historical selection." So, this book has been published for more than 220 years, and the book often contains annotations, proving that what he said is indeed credible. Presumably, the author wanted to popularize the great achievements of overseas colonization in the past thirty-seven years to the people, and on the other hand, he wanted to gain the trust and acceptance of the scholar-officials, so he wrote it in a special style. However, there is one doubt: when he wrote this book, Kangxi was not dead yet, so he should not have called him the "Holy Ancestor." Or perhaps Chen's preface is fake.

From his annotations, we know that Risheng's father, Meiao, followed the Earl of Yongsheng Zheng Cai to serve as a supervisor on the river with Hongguang, and later served as a general with the seal of Longxiang. He returned to the Qing Dynasty in the year of Dingji. So he was also a remnant of the Ming Dynasty, so he did not dare to miss the former master, so he had to miss the heroes of the isolated island. However, between the lines, it has already been polished smoothly and roundly, and everywhere is an expression of a compliant subject.

The entire book has thirty volumes, and each volume has a seven-character chapter title. The parallelism is not neat, such as "General Shi discusses leaving Taiwan, and the Great Qing Dynasty has peace in the four seas." It can be seen that he is not very familiar with the writing methods of chapter-style novels, so he does not even use conclusions like "If you want to know what will happen next, listen to the next chapter."

There are several transliterated words in Chinese. Some come from English, such as "赤般" (Chiban), which is said to be a ship name, probably "Ship." Others include "哔吱," "哆囉呢," etc. It even mentions that the Japanese were afraid of the Tang people along the coast and even removed the rudders of large and small ships, not allowing "unfilial Japanese people to go abroad to rebel." How long ago was it that Taiwan, which had been hard-earned, was handed over to the "unfilial Japanese people." Not only that, but it also had to be added to the "old nest of the Great Qing Dynasty" of "peace in the four seas." How can we not be indignant when we read this book?

I think this book is worth giving a new look and reprinting. It's more meaningful than just shouting slogans to recover lost territory.

Poets and Wine 250

— Yong Wen

Because of the saying "Wine can delight my nature, and poetry can express my feelings," poets since ancient times, with the exception of Wang Anshi, who did not understand the "poetic and wine affair," have been immersed in alcohol all day long, living their "one spring spends a long time buying flowers, and every day I sleep drunk next to the flowers," "I sleep when I'm drunk and drink when I'm awake; what's the point if I'm not crazy?" life of "poetic and drunken extravagance."

As soon as poets see wine, they reveal the appearance of "drooling at the sight of a wine cart on the road," wishing they could "get drunk today if there is wine today, and empty the limited cup in front of me," even if they are fortunate enough to be summoned by the emperor, they still recite "The emperor calls me, but I won't get on the boat. I claim to be a wine immortal," naturally disobeying the imperial edict in the identity of a "wine immortal." Therefore, in the eyes of poets, they only hope "three hundred and sixty days a year, drunk as mud every day," ignoring everything else, and still saying, "The universe is vast in drunkenness" and "Getting drunk for twenty-nine days a month is better than being awake for twenty-nine days for the world!"

The "wine desire" of poets is truly fully expressed. Look, they drink wine for farewell: "A cup of wine comforts the parting face"; they drink wine for leaving: "Wanting to go but not going, let's empty our cups"; they drink wine while talking: "Talking about mulberry and hemp with wine"; even how long they stay at the homes of relatives and friends is determined by whether there is wine or not: "But if the host can make the guest drunk, he doesn't know where his hometown is!" Other things such as climbing mountains and playing in the water, they must "drink three hundred cups" and "first try to get drunk as mud."

Poets are mostly prone to melancholy, so they want to express the complaint of "There is nowhere to go after drinking this body." Therefore, drinking "goose yellow" (yellow wine) is also a manifestation of trying to forget their worries! Otherwise, why say: "How to relieve worries? Only with strong wine"? And why would they write poems like "A five-flower horse, a thousand-gold fur coat, call the boy to take it out and exchange it for fine wine, and drink it with you to dispel all the sorrows of eternity," "float this thing to forget worries," "a drunken solution to a thousand sorrows," and "Tears are separated in the cup, how to send tears into a sorrowful heart?"

The most famous wine drinker among poets, everyone knows, is Li Bai. If you don't believe me, look at the horizontal plaque "Legacy of Taibai" hanging in the wine shop, and you can know the great amount of wine Taibai drank. But Chen Xuan, who wished people to inscribe his tomb after his death with "The Spirit Path of Chen Jun, the Former Wine Friend of Liang," and Liu Ling, who wrote "Ode to Wine Virtue," and Tao Qian, who prefaced "Drinking Poems," were not weak in their alcohol consumption either!

Shao Yuanchong, Cao Xiangheng, Mao Heting and other celebrities in Beijing, as the old man Sanyuan also happened to come to Beijing, held an elegant gathering on the Double Ninth Festival of the old calendar, chosen to be held in the Saoyelou. It is said that more than sixty celebrities in the capital were invited, which was a grand occasion for a while. It is said that the old man Sanyuan intends to give a poem "Resistance to Frost." The old man has abandoned the matter of chanting poems for a long time because of illness. This is especially a good story for the art world. Cheng immediately set off to Shanghai the next day.

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast Army 252

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seventeen: Who Can Be Heartless? Home Thoughts Gray the Morale; Soldiers Despise Not Deception, Brave Words Boost the Army's Spirit

Now that the battalion commander has mentioned letting him go back to Haidian to find a car, his heart suddenly moved. Isn't this an excellent opportunity to go home? Even if something in the camp is delayed, he can use the excuse of going out on official business. Thinking like this, he said to Battalion Commander Bao, "In that case, I'll go to Haidian and try to find one." Anyway, if I can't find a four-legged animal, is there anything I can't find among two-legged people?" Bao Fang smiled and said, "You can kill two birds with one stone. Going back to see your fiancée is much better than squeezing time to go back yourself, right? Actually, don't be so stupid and go looking for it yourself. Take a few brothers with you, and have the quartermaster follow along. You let them go out and look, and you stay at home and talk to the old man for a few words. Then, find your lady and sit in the milk tea shop, eating, drinking, and talking for two or three hours. Everything will be ready, and you can return to the camp in a grand manner. Wouldn't that be fun?" Zhao Ziqiang smiled wryly and said, "Battalion commander, do you think this is still fun?" Bao Fang laughed and said, "You don't need to say anything else. Hurry back." After this consideration, Zhao Ziqiang already felt eager to return home. Since the battalion commander was urging him, what was he delaying? So, he went back to the company headquarters, called the quartermaster to take a few brothers, and they went to Haidian together. Today, when he passed through that wilderness, he didn't know loneliness, and he didn't know sorrow. Naturally, there was no joy. He walked forward in such confusion. When he arrived on the street, he pointed out a few ways to the quartermaster and asked him to find a car. He walked home alone. When he walked toward his home, he naturally strode forward, but when he arrived at the gate, his legs suddenly felt weak and he couldn't lift them. The door was closed. He was about to reach out to knock on the door knocker, but when he was four or five inches away, he retracted his hand. He thought that he could say anything to his father. But if he met this new mother-in-law and told her that he was about to leave for Xifengkou, wouldn't that be like punching her in the chest? When he saw her face, he should hide it and not say it, right? Thinking like this, standing at the gate, he couldn't help but hesitate. (225)

Grain: Imported Wheat Quotes Lead to Decline in Marked Flour 267

Yesterday, after the flour market opened in the morning, prices for all months uniformly showed a declining trend. The quotes for imported wheat from Chicago fell by 8-9 jiao to 1 yuan, and those from Canada fell by around 5-6 jiao. Therefore, sentiment became unstable immediately after the opening. The continuous rise in prices in recent days seemed to be largely driven by foreign markets. Now that foreign markets have fallen, it is difficult for the market to remain strong. Opening prices were already 2 fen lower than the previous day, and prices continued to fluctuate. By the time the afternoon market opened, the current month was still showing weakness. However, due to indications of purchases by mills, the decline was weaker. November and December saw less of a decline due to fewer offerings. However, prices for January and later months fell sharply because a certain mill had been gradually offering stock, and it was rumored that Australian wheat prices were favorable, at around 4.5 yuan. Observing the subsequent trend, if imported wheat quotes decline, the market is expected to remain weak. Otherwise, a stable situation is expected. As a result, the current month fell by 3.25 li compared to the previous day, November fell by 2 fen, December fell by 1.75 li, January fell by 4 fen, and February and March fell by 4.25 li.

Distant Month Wheat Follows Imported Wheat Decline. Current Month Uniquely Strong Due to Delivery Products Being Purchased by Mills 268

Yesterday, after the forward wheat market opened in the morning, all months showed a decline. The quotes for imported wheat from Chicago fell by 8-9 jiao to 1 yuan, and those from Canada fell by 5-6 jiao. Therefore, sentiment was uniformly unstable after the opening, and selling pressure was quite strong. Prices for all months fell by 2-3-4 fen compared to the previous day. Free Talk

Chinese Writing and the Chinese People 276

— Yu Ming

Recently, a very good translation was published: "The Chinese Language and Chinese Writing" by Bernhard Karlgren. Mr. Karlgren is a Swede. His real name is Karlgren. Why is he "surnamed" Gao? That is undoubtedly because he has become Sinicized. He has indeed made great contributions to Chinese philology.

However, he seems to have more research on the Chinese people. Therefore, he admires classical Chinese and Chinese characters, believing that they are indispensable for the Chinese people.

He said: "Recently [note: Mr. Gao's book was published in London in 1923], some newspapers have tried to use vernacular Chinese, but they have not been very successful; therefore, perhaps they will also anger most subscribers, believing that this is implying that they cannot understand classical Chinese newspapers!"

"In Western countries, there are many actors who can insert many 'jokes' at almost any time during their performances, and there are also many authors who overuse literary quotations; but everyone recognizes this as an inferior style. In China, the opposite is true; this is considered a high-level elegance and a display of exquisite skill."

The "ambiguity of Chinese writing not only does not cause difficulties for the Chinese people, but they are willing to cultivate it."

However, Mr. Gao himself has suffered enough humiliation because of this: "The author of this book can fully understand what is said to him when he talks with dear Chinese people; but when they talk to each other, he hardly understands a word." This is naturally those "dear Chinese people" "implying" that he does not understand the language of the upper class because "foreigners who come to China only need to pay attention to one point, and he can feel that although he is familiar with the language of ordinary people, he is still confused about the conversations of the upper class."

So he said: "Chinese writing is like a beautiful and lovely noblewoman, and Western writing is like a useful but ugly servant."

The "exquisite skill" of the beautiful, lovely, and useless noblewoman lies in the ambiguity of "inserting jokes." This makes the best Western scholars at most equal to ordinary people in China, and they cannot hope to climb into the upper class. In this way, we have "spiritually triumphed." In order to maintain this victory, we must have a sophisticated and elegant vocabulary, and it must be rich! The "lack of great success" of the May Fourth vernacular movement was largely due to the upper class fearing that people would imply that they did not understand classical Chinese.

Although, "This is one right, and that is another right!" [We] might as well be more ambiguous. Otherwise, we will suffer difficulties instead.

Look Again |Continuing to Talk About Wrongly Written Characters| 277

— Cao Juren

An American scientist named Slosson once calculated that if the person who first created the word "Electric" had simply combined it with two or three letters, he did not know how much he would save in pens, ink, writing effort, and typesetting effort. But our Mr. Tao Tiran is worried about my surname, fearing that writing it as "Curved Sun Cao," missing a stroke, would lose some dignity. Whenever there is a reform of writing, it is always intellectuals who claim to know some square characters who come out to oppose it; this is nothing more than fearing that the general public will gain the opportunity to use writing, and that their only skill will completely lose its effectiveness and have to be relearned, and they are afraid of relearning. The subconscious mind of mocking young people for writing wrongly and the psychology of cherishing writing are consistent. (When Turkey implemented writing reform, the opposition from intellectuals was the strongest; there were also many intellectuals who opposed the national phonetic alphabet and the Roman alphabet: knowing more square characters is the only property of intellectuals, so the fear of loss is the greatest.)

Professor Whitney said: "Writing does not belong to individuals, but to each member of society... What each of us wants to say cannot become language and writing until everyone adopts it. The entire development of language begins with individuals, but is completed by society." Therefore, writing is a common currency. No one will be willing to use the banknotes of a bankrupt bank. Reading wrongly written characters and writing wrongly written characters is not an accidental phenomenon. In the past and present, people of all colors, high, middle, and low, have done so. If we do not follow the trend to seek remedies, such as constantly correcting them as Mr. Tiran advocates, then the "Explanation of Characters" states: "Immersion follows reason." This immersion character. "Lecherous" states: "Private abandonment." Adultery states: "Committing lechery." This chaste lecherous character. "May I ask, Mr. Tiran, can you grab every scholar and tell them, 'Lecherous should be written as lecherous'?" The Qi Li Long in the middle of the Qiantang River, this "Long" should be pronounced "Shuang": May I ask, Mr. Tiran, can you grab passersby and tell them, "Long should be pronounced Shuang"? During the Jiaqing period of the Qing Dynasty, a certain official stated that "the people in the capital call Xuanwu Gate Shunzhi Gate, Zhengyang Gate Qian Gate, and Chongwen Gate Hada Gate. It is appropriate to order them to correct it." The emperor ordered him to start correcting them from a certain day at the Qian Gate when he met people. Mr. Tiran is enthusiastic about correcting wrongly written characters, and I want to copy this and go to correct them when I meet people! (For example, "this one" should be "zhe ge," the "ran" in "tiran" is the "burn" character, and the "burn" character should not be used separately; the "clown" character "chou" should be written as the "cuan" character.)

Writing wrongly written characters and reading wrongly written characters is not without rules. In 70-80% of cases, there is a relationship in sound, either the same consonant (partial alliteration or alliteration) or the same vowel; such as "wrongly written character" written as "blank character," "wrong" and "blank" are alliterative, "hearth" is written as "ugly," "hearth" and "ugly" are alliterative. In the remaining 20-30% of cases, there is a relationship in the shape of the characters, mostly simplification; such as "tofu" written as "dou fu," "one head of cattle" written as "one bean of cattle," "yin yang" written as "yin yi," "a hair's breadth" written as "a hair's width." Following the first trend, Chinese writing can be completely transformed into new phono-semantic characters; following the second trend, Chinese writing can be completely transformed into simplified characters. The social reading of wrongly written characters and the writing of wrongly written characters is the precursor to reforming Chinese writing, which is why I have to look again.

As for theoretical discussions, I will write another long article and ask Mr. Tiran for guidance. (To be published in the 75th issue of Tao Sound)

Sun Yuanru and Huang Zhongze 278

— Zhu Xia

Huang Zhongze had extensive social interactions during his life, and Sun Yuanru was one of them. In the past, after reading Yuanru's "Cheng Qing Tang Drafts," I saw in the poems he wrote for Zhongze that their friendship was very close, and there was also a lot of historical material about Zhongze. Statistically, there are the following poems: (1) On Huang Er's Collection of Huangshan Mountain Paintings, (2) Composed with Huang Er Jingren during a Boat Trip in Runzhou, (3) Boating with Yang San (Lun), Hong Da (Liangji), and Huang Er (Jingren) to See Lotuses at Pingshan Hall, (4) Huang Er Jingren Returned from a Trip to Huangshan Mountain and Requested a Long Poem as a Gift, (5) Answering Hong Da's Work After Being Drunk, Simultaneously Thinking of Huang Zhongze, (6) Hong Da Asked for a Title for a Painting of Yunxi Melody, Along with a Shadow of Huang Da Jingren. From these poem titles alone, we can obtain some material. Among these poems, the one about "Huang Er Jingren's Return from a Trip to Huangshan Mountain and Requesting a Long Poem as a Gift" contains the most historical information. Although this poem is inevitably a social obligation, it can very well serve as a conclusion to Zhongze's southern travels. Zhongze's character, circumstances, family, and even his friendship with Yuanru, as well as his satisfaction after returning from his southern travels, are all visible in it. In other poems, such as "Seeing Lotuses at Pingshan Hall," which contains the line "One child knocks on the side of the boat, two children sing, my hand does not release the golden goblet," and the poem "Thinking of Zhongze," which contains the lines "The joys of life are like sparks of flint, after parting, tears fall in vain," and the poem "Hong Da Asked for a Title," which contains the lines "Not worried about the purple deer damaging the white fur coat, but only afraid that the mirrored pool will not reflect a beautiful face," as well as what is said in the poem "Huangshan Mountain Paintings," "After Huang Sheng left, the mountain colors died, clear water and white stones sadly trickled. Standing up straight, pointing out old places of play, entering and exiting, high and low, exploring difficulties," all of these can also be used as reference materials for Zhongze's history.

Words from Paradise 279

— Yi Cen

A very good friend from the past, after several years of separation, I hadn't received any news. Yesterday, I suddenly received a letter from him. He said he envied me living in this paradise-like metropolis and imagined I was living a very carefree life. He also told me not to forget him and asked me to introduce him to a job.

After reading this letter once, I couldn't help but smile bitterly for a while. I should have replied to him immediately, but I really didn't have the courage. Because what should I write on the letter in reply? If I truthfully told him about my recent situation, if he believed me, I was afraid it would greatly disappoint this friend I hadn't seen for many years. Or it might even cause him to feel some undeserved sadness for me. If he didn't believe me, then I was afraid it would cause him to misunderstand me and spread some gossip about me. Caught in such a dilemma, after some deliberation, I finally decided to reply to the letter. But the letter only described the scenes of being together with him in the past, and many past events, in vivid words. I said: In my life, I am afraid that only the past time was worthy of what you called "a very carefree life." Because at that time, I had just entered society, and I was naive and inexperienced. I didn't fully understand all the difficulties of life!

I also wrote: Do you envy me living in this paradise-like place? Indeed, this place is truly like paradise, with tall Western-style houses and wide roads. And on the roads, one can constantly see endlessly flowing, recklessly driving cars, inside which sit some foreign gentlemen and ladies. Relying on the protection of airplanes and warships, they transport all kinds of novel goods, cheat countless amounts of money from the Chinese people, and enjoy themselves.

There are also some special class of locals sitting in the cars, who are equally imposing and luxurious. Because they rely on their own abilities, or the opportunities given to them by their fathers, to exploit and plunder, and have made huge fortunes!

There are also women here whose numbers are constantly increasing, who live by selling their bodies, with faces covered in fragrant powder, wearing silk clothes, and being so charming and sensual that they bewitch people!

There are also speculators who arise in response to the times, who are good at understanding people's intentions, catering to fashion, and establishing numerous theaters, dance halls, ... countless alluring money pits!

As for the lives of other people in the paradise-like place he imagined, I never told him about it. Because I knew that when the other side of the situation was written out, it would definitely not be as lively as the front. Anyway, we are all people born in this era. Is it possible that there will never be a time when he understands?

Two Brothers (11) 280

— By Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

Ten minutes later, they were having dinner in the small dining room downstairs.

At first, everyone was silent; but after a while, old man Roland began to question the notary's visit again.

"Why didn't he write a letter and come in person?"

Pierre found this very natural.

"It must be because he needs an answer immediately; and perhaps he has some secret clauses to tell us, and people don't like to write letters about this."

But the four people in the Roland family were still speculating about this, and all four felt in their hearts that they shouldn't have invited this irrelevant woman to dinner, making it inconvenient for them to argue and decide everything.

They had just returned to the living room on the second floor when the maid announced that the notary had arrived.

Roland hurried over.

"Good evening, dear Master (Maitre)."

He gave Mr. Lecarre the honorific title of "Master," which was originally attached to the names of all notaries.

Mrs. Lusuimi stood up and said:

"I'm going back, I'm very tired."

Everyone tried to persuade her to stay a little; but she was determined not to, so she left alone, unlike usual, when one of the three men would always accompany her.

Mrs. Roland hurriedly approached the new guest:

"Would you like a cup of coffee?"

"No, thank you, I just had dinner."

"Then, how about a cup of tea?"

"I won't say no, but a little later, let's talk about business first."

After the notary said these two sentences, everyone was silent, and only the rhythmic ticking of the clock and the sound of the maid washing pots downstairs were heard. This maid was so stupid that she wouldn't even eavesdrop outside the door.

The notary spoke again:

"Do you know a Mr. Marais in Paris, a Mr. Rene Marais?"

The Roland couple made the same exclamation of surprise: Indeed, they did!

"Is this a friend of yours?"

Roland said:

"A very good friend. But this is a Paris fanatic; he never wants to leave the streets of Paris. He is a director in the Ministry of Finance. I haven't seen him since I left the capital. And we haven't had any news for a long time. You understand, when we are very far apart..."

The notary said seriously:

"Mr. Marais has passed away."

Both the man and the woman had this small gesture of sorrow and surprise, which, whether feigned or real, people always immediately show when they receive such news. (To be continued)

Commentary

The Ladder of Life 281

— Li Qi

The means of livelihood for the more than three million residents of Shanghai are like a ladder. The layers are so numerous and excessive that they far surpass the Four-Bank Warehouse, which has not yet been fully constructed! Some people say that prostitutes lead a hellish life. In fact, in Shanghai, where the layers of life are so disparate, the lives of prostitutes are still considered to be in the middle and lower layers of many layers of hell!

Now, let's imitate the way of "climbing step by step" and exhibit the lives of Shanghai people, starting from the lowest layer, counting down step by step, and occasionally displaying them in parallel:

Below the basic point, one must naturally count those beggars who emit miserable cries in the streets and alleys, or strike their own bodies with bricks and tiles, or lead dogs to kneel at doors, or roll around the streets with mutilated limbs, risking a few drops of blood and hoarse cries in exchange for copper coins. Others who knock on clappers and oil drum buckets and sing from door to door are slightly "higher." As for the "Jiao Hua Tou," they should be considered to be "living in the attic" of the beggar layer, because there are still two or three layers below him.

One level "higher" should be the lumpenproletariat. Under this general term, there are also many levels to be divided. The most basic is the "Bi San Young Master," who wanders on the streets and eaves of houses, barely hanging a miserable smile on their sallow faces, begging for cold leftovers from various catering establishments. "Above," there are pickpockets and thieves; there are vendors of erotic paintings who take the Fourth Road as their base; there are "guides" for "swallow nests," "mirror polishers," and "Russian halls" ("clear water girls") who haunt North Sichuan Road and Aidoa Road; there are low-level rogues who sit in teahouses and haggle over prices; there are various nomadic peddlers; there are "tycoons" who dominate a street. Going step by step from the "tycoon" line, "Nine Turns Reviving Elixir," after several cultivations, you can keep rising to XX.

To the right of the lumpenproletariat are the formal proletarians: there are coolies who often treat cement as "Simmons" and burlap sacks as "coats," there are rickshaw pullers, there are apprentices who take "eating a living" and emptying chamber pots as their "central task," there are small workers; there are handicraft workers, there are industrial workers. Once they reach the foreman and clerk, they completely change their nature and become the capitalist's "paw layer," no longer proletarians.

One level "higher" are shop assistants. From apprentices, senior clerks, leaving the store, traveling salesmen, storefronts, accounting rooms, etc., the highest level of which has a life no less than that of middle-class freelancers, and the lowest level is as miserable as workers.

One level "higher" than shop assistants are small and medium-sized merchants. They are also divided into several levels: from the owners of sesame cake and fried dough stick shops and tofu shops, to small cigarette paper shops and grocery stores, rising in order of capital amount. When they reach company managers or have huge sums of money deposited in banks, they must be "evaluated" separately and not regarded as "bosses" anymore.

There is another level, which is freelancers. Starting from elementary school teachers who receive six or eight yuan a month in "stipends," clerks who earn fifteen to thirty yuan a month, the group of writers who sell words for rice, and the technical personnel of various organizations... rising in order, until "famous doctors" and "great lawyers" who earn thirty thousand or twenty thousand taels a month. The layers within this general term are four times as complex as "streaky pork"! In fact, teachers and low-level clerks who receive salaries below the standard, as well as nameless writers who are often hungry and use their brains to create wealth for book merchants, should all be called "long-gown workers." Their economic status and life pain are "two fives equal ten" with the working masses. The most popular famous doctors and great lawyers often also operate real estate or hold stocks, and are genuine bourgeoisie. The most depressed and often "pretending to be fat when their faces are swollen" are a large group in between "long-gown workers" and the above-mentioned capitalists who "moonlight": always rising and sinking, circling in the journey of life, worrying about gains and losses.

Going further up are the compradors, bureaucrats, and industrial or financial bourgeoisie. If they are good at dancing with long sleeves and climb further up, they will become "great" and be listed in the daily life notes of "officials coming and going" in Beijing and Shanghai. At the same time,
